\section{Direct finite extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{Lstar}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the current stage, the carrier-side longitudinal problem is a literal finite
matrix-element calculation.

The enriched shell carrier is already fixed as
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\},
\]
and the projected core block has the explicit valley form
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore the remaining longitudinal audit reduces to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the two \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrices \(E_\pm(0)\),
\item diagonalize them and extract the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\),
\item compute
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1),
\]
\item compute the shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix
\[
U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\]
\item extract
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3 U_\parallel),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining frontier is finite and explicit.

\section{1. Explicit \(2\times2\) valley blocks}

Write the two valley-diagonal projected matrices as general Hermitian matrices:
\begin{equation}
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Epm_general}
\end{equation}
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

Define the trace/difference data
\begin{equation}
t_\pm:=\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2},
\qquad
d_\pm:=\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2},
\qquad
\rho_\pm:=|c_\pm|.
\label{eq:tpmdpm}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
E_\pm(0)
=
t_\pm \mathbf 1_2
+
d_\pm \Sigma_3
+
(\Re c_\pm)\Sigma_1
-
(\Im c_\pm)\Sigma_2.
\label{eq:Epm_Pauli}
\end{equation}

Its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low/high})}
=
t_\pm
\mp
R_\pm,
\qquad
R_\pm:=\sqrt{d_\pm^2+\rho_\pm^2}.
\label{eq:eigs_Epm}
\end{equation}
The low internal carrier state is therefore the normalized eigenvector of
\(\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}=t_\pm-R_\pm\).

\section{2. Explicit normalized low eigenvectors}

Let
\begin{equation}
c_\pm=\rho_\pm e^{i\phi_\pm},
\qquad
\rho_\pm\ge 0.
\label{eq:c_phase}
\end{equation}
Introduce the Bloch-sphere angle \(\theta_\pm\) by
\begin{equation}
\cos\theta_\pm=\frac{d_\pm}{R_\pm},
\qquad
\sin\theta_\pm=\frac{\rho_\pm}{R_\pm},
\qquad
0\le \theta_\pm\le \pi.
\label{eq:theta_pm_def}
\end{equation}

A convenient normalized low eigenvector choice is
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm
=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\,e^{-i\phi_\pm}\sin(\theta_\pm/2)\\
\cos(\theta_\pm/2)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:eta_pm_spinor}
\end{equation}
up to an irrelevant overall phase.
Equivalently, in component notation,
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(\pm)}\\
A_2^{(\pm)}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
|A_1^{(\pm)}|^2+|A_2^{(\pm)}|^2=1.
\label{eq:eta_comp}
\end{equation}

If one wants a formula directly from the matrix entries without spherical angles, one may also use
\begin{equation}
r_\pm:=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{d_\pm+R_\pm},
\label{eq:r_pm}
\end{equation}
whenever \(d_\pm+R_\pm\neq 0\), and then
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{1+|r_\pm|^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
r_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:eta_rform}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Closed formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
\label{eq:Delta_def_main}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:eta_pm_spinor}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
e^{\,i(\phi_+-\phi_-)}
\sin\frac{\theta_+}{2}\sin\frac{\theta_-}{2}
-
\cos\frac{\theta_+}{2}\cos\frac{\theta_-}{2}.
\label{eq:Delta_angle_form}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, with the ratio form \eqref{eq:eta_rform},
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
\label{eq:Delta_ratio_form}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact vanishing condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:Delta_zero_condition}
\end{equation}

This is very useful:
\(\Delta_{00}\) vanishes only when the two low valley eigenvectors satisfy a very specific
matching relation.
So unless an exact symmetry enforces \(\overline{r_+}r_-=1\), the generic expectation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_generic}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Reduced shell-normal \(J\)-matrix and \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

Define
\begin{equation}
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)=\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
\label{eq:Uparallel_def}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
u_\parallel
=
\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
\label{eq:uparallel_diag_formula}
\end{equation}

Now decompose \(U_\parallel\) in the Pauli basis:
\begin{equation}
U_\parallel
=
u_0 \mathbf 1_2
+
u_1\Sigma_1
+
u_2\Sigma_2
+
u_3\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:Uparallel_Pauli}
\end{equation}
Then immediately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel=u_3.
}
\label{eq:uparallel_u3}
\end{equation}

So the carrier-side longitudinal scalar does not depend on the full \(2\times2\) matrix.
It depends only on the \(\Sigma_3\)-component of the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-block.

This is the key simplification.

\section{5. Closed formula for \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{Lstar}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\label{eq:Lstar_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:uparallel_diag_formula},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_diag}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:uparallel_u3},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_3.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_u3}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact vanishing criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_3=0.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_zero_cond}
\end{equation}

Therefore, once \(m_\parallel\neq 0\), the only way the longitudinal slot dies is that the
shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-block becomes exactly \(\Sigma_3\)-symmetric in its diagonal entries.

\section{6. Minimal executable protocol}

The full carrier-side longitudinal audit is now algorithmically closed.

\subsection*{Step 1}
Compute the two valley blocks
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\subsection*{Step 2}
Compute
\[
R_\pm=\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2},
\qquad
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}=\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}-R_\pm.
\]

\subsection*{Step 3}
Construct the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) from either
\eqref{eq:eta_pm_spinor} or \eqref{eq:eta_rform}.

\subsection*{Step 4}
Evaluate
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-.
\]

\subsection*{Step 5}
Compute the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\[
U_\parallel=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\]
and extract
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)=\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
\]

\subsection*{Step 6}
Read off
\[
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

\subsection*{Step 7}
Apply the practical sufficient condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:practical_suff_final}
\end{equation}
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:ultramin_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest theorem-level status}

What has now been fully reduced is not merely the existence statement, but the exact finite audit map:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0),E_-(0),U_\parallel,m_\parallel)
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*).
}
\label{eq:finite_map}
\end{equation}

What is still not inserted numerically is the actual microscopic value of the entries
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel.
\]

So the only remaining honest open part is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final microscopic matrix-element insertion, not the reduction logic.}
}
\]

\section{Final summary}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal problem is a finite \(2\times2\) matrix audit.

Write
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
U_\parallel=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) of \(E_\pm(0)\) determine
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-.
}
\]

Equivalently, if
\[
r_\pm=-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\]

The shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias is
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Therefore the carrier-side longitudinal witness is controlled by
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
}
\]
up to the explicit remainder \(R_N\).

Hence the practical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\]

So the longitudinal frontier is no longer structural.
It is reduced to the final insertion of the actual microscopic entries of
\(E_\pm(0)\), \(U_\parallel\), and \(m_\parallel\).

\section{Direct finite extraction of the remaining longitudinal scalars}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is a literal finite
\(2\times2\) matrix problem.

The enriched shell carrier is already fixed as
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\},
\]
and the projected core block is
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore the final longitudinal audit reduces to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the two Hermitian \(2\times2\) valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\),
\item diagonalize them to obtain the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\),
\item extract
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1),
\]
\item compute the shell-normal intervalley matrix
\[
U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\]
\item extract
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining problem is finite and explicit.

\section{1. Explicit \(2\times2\) valley blocks}

Write the two valley-diagonal projected blocks as general Hermitian matrices:
\begin{equation}
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Epm_general}
\end{equation}
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

Define
\begin{equation}
t_\pm:=\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2},
\qquad
d_\pm:=\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2},
\qquad
\rho_\pm:=|c_\pm|.
\label{eq:tpmdpm}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
E_\pm(0)
=
t_\pm \mathbf 1_2
+
d_\pm \Sigma_3
+
(\Re c_\pm)\Sigma_1
-
(\Im c_\pm)\Sigma_2.
\label{eq:Epm_pauli}
\end{equation}

Thus the nontrivial part of each valley block is encoded in the Bloch vector
\[
\mathbf h_\pm
=
(\Re c_\pm,\,-\Im c_\pm,\,d_\pm).
\]

\section{2. Low eigenvalues and normalized low eigenvectors}

The eigenvalues of \(E_\pm(0)\) are
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low/high})}
=
t_\pm \mp R_\pm,
\qquad
R_\pm:=\sqrt{d_\pm^2+\rho_\pm^2}.
\label{eq:eigs}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
c_\pm=\rho_\pm e^{i\phi_\pm},
\qquad
\rho_\pm\ge 0.
\label{eq:cphase}
\end{equation}
Introduce the polar angle \(\theta_\pm\) by
\begin{equation}
\cos\theta_\pm=\frac{d_\pm}{R_\pm},
\qquad
\sin\theta_\pm=\frac{\rho_\pm}{R_\pm}.
\label{eq:theta_def}
\end{equation}

A convenient normalized low eigenvector choice is
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm
=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\,e^{-i\phi_\pm}\sin(\theta_\pm/2)\\
\cos(\theta_\pm/2)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:eta_angle}
\end{equation}
up to an overall phase.

Equivalently, in component form,
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(\pm)}\\
A_2^{(\pm)}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
|A_1^{(\pm)}|^2+|A_2^{(\pm)}|^2=1.
\label{eq:eta_comp}
\end{equation}

A completely algebraic expression is obtained by setting
\begin{equation}
r_\pm
:=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{d_\pm+R_\pm},
\label{eq:rpm}
\end{equation}
whenever \(d_\pm+R_\pm\neq 0\), and then
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{1+|r_\pm|^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
r_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:eta_r}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact extraction formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
\label{eq:Delta_def}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:eta_angle}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
e^{i(\phi_+-\phi_-)}
\sin\frac{\theta_+}{2}\sin\frac{\theta_-}{2}
-
\cos\frac{\theta_+}{2}\cos\frac{\theta_-}{2}.
\label{eq:Delta_angle}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:eta_r}, one gets the more algebraic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_r}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact vanishing condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:Delta_zero}
\end{equation}

This is important.
It shows that \(\Delta_{00}\) does \emph{not} vanish generically.
Its vanishing requires a very specific matching relation between the two low-valley eigenvectors.

Therefore, unless an exact symmetry or exact microscopic tuning enforces
\(\overline{r_+}r_-=1\), the generic expectation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_generic}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact extraction formula for \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

Define the shell-normal reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\begin{equation}
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)=\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
\label{eq:Uparallel_def}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:uparallel_diag}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, expand \(U_\parallel\) in the Pauli basis:
\begin{equation}
U_\parallel
=
u_0\mathbf 1_2
+
u_1\Sigma_1
+
u_2\Sigma_2
+
u_3\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:Uparallel_pauli}
\end{equation}
Then immediately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel=u_3.
}
\label{eq:uparallel_u3}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal scalar depends only on the \(\Sigma_3\)-component of the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix.

\section{5. Exact extraction formula for \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{Lstar}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\label{eq:Lstar_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:uparallel_diag},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_diag}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:uparallel_u3},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_3.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_u3}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact vanishing criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_3=0.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus, once \(m_\parallel\neq 0\), the only way the longitudinal slot dies is the exact diagonal cancellation
\[
u_{11}=u_{22}.
\]

Again, this is not generic.
It is a codimension-one cancellation inside the shell-normal intervalley block.

\section{6. Combined practical sufficient condition}

The carrier-side longitudinal witness is controlled by the dominant product
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
\label{eq:dominant_product}
\end{equation}
up to the explicit harmonic remainder \(R_N\).

Therefore the practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:practical_suff}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:ultramin}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Delta_r} and \eqref{eq:Lstar_diag}, one may rewrite this explicitly as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}
\right|
\cdot
|\alpha_X|
\cdot
\left|
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})
\right|
\cdot
|A_{G_*}|
>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:fully_explicit_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest conclusion}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is no longer structural.

It is completely reduced to the finite microscopic insertion of the entries
\[
a_\pm,\quad b_\pm,\quad c_\pm,\quad
u_{11},\quad u_{22},\quad
m_\parallel.
\]

Once those are computed from the actual projected refined locked Bloch operator, the longitudinal decision is immediate.

In particular:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Delta_{00}\) is nonzero unless the two low-valley eigenvectors satisfy the exact tuned relation
\[
\overline{r_+}r_-=1;
\]

\item \(L_*\) is nonzero unless either \(m_\parallel=0\) or the shell-normal intervalley diagonal asymmetry cancels exactly:
\[
u_{11}=u_{22}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining open part is not a theorem-level reduction.
It is only the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of these finite matrix elements.

\section{Final summary}

The carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the finite extraction of two scalars:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

Write the two valley blocks as
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2}.
\]

Define
\[
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
\]
Then the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) give
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\]

Next define the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\[
U_\parallel
=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\]

The practical sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus no structural ambiguity remains.
Only the explicit symbolic or numerical insertion of the finite projected matrix entries
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel
\]
remains.

\section{1. Explicit reduced longitudinal coefficient}

\lambda_\parallel

I_{\theta'^3}

This is already a fully explicit finite expression.

Equation \eqref{eq:lambda_fully_explicit} immediately gives two exact subcases.

\subsection{B. Pure mediated branch}

\end{equation}

So the mediated branch is also closed.

Generically,
\begin{equation}

\end{equation}

So at the reduced longitudinal-coefficient level, the honest situation is already much stronger than “structure only”:

\section{Strategic Summary for Breaking the Full-PDE Bottleneck}

\item the dynamical existence and global matching of the defect background.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the orthodox strategy is not to delay everything until a fully unique microscopic PDE is derived.
Instead, one should adopt the strongest explicit working branch and elevate only the unresolved pieces to sharply formulated assumptions with finite verification targets.

A minimal working package is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item refined locked \(+\) Class II microscopic branch,
\item existence of a shell-/defect-adapted Callias-admissible background,
\item actual longitudinal carrier survival:

\]
\item optional background-field FRG completion for derivative isotropy:
\[
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathrm{traceless}})<0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The highest-return immediate move is not another abstract PDE theorem,
but the explicit 12-mode BCC Bloch / shell construction:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to

\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

In particular, the carrier-side bottleneck is already reduced to the finite longitudinal basis-overlap audit
\[

\]

Thus the right pivot is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{replace the monolithic full-PDE demand by a working-branch theorem package plus finite audits.}
}

\section{Can working assumptions become naturally discharged later?}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Yes, but not automatically.

A working assumption is useful only if, after pushing the derivation forward,
it is transformed into one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a finite coefficient-extraction problem,
\item a codimension-one non-cancellation condition,
\item a variational existence problem,
\item an RG/fixed-point stability condition.
\end{enumerate}

If this happens, then the assumption is not merely a permanent postulate.
It becomes a \emph{dischargeable hypothesis}.

If, on the contrary, the assumption remains a broad structural declaration even after the entire derivation is pushed through, then it has not been reduced and remains a genuine independent postulate.

Thus the right question is not:
\[
\text{``Can we assume it for now?''}
\]
but rather:
\[
\text{``Does this assumption reduce, later, to an explicit verification problem?''}
\]

\section{1. General principle}

Suppose a theorem package is built from a set of working assumptions
\[
\mathcal A_1,\mathcal A_2,\dots,\mathcal A_n.
\]
There are three logically distinct outcomes.

\subsection*{Type I: reducible assumptions}
An assumption \(\mathcal A_k\) is reducible if the forward derivation converts it into a finite or sharply formulated check:
\[
\mathcal A_k
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{explicit finite test / spectral test / overlap test}.
\]
Such an assumption is often only provisional.
Later it may be discharged by direct calculation.

\subsection*{Type II: genericity assumptions}
An assumption is of genericity type if the forward derivation shows that its failure requires exact tuning:
\[
\mathcal A_k \text{ fails }
\iff
\text{a codimension-one or higher cancellation condition holds}.
\]
Then the assumption is not fully proved, but it is strengthened:
its negation is non-generic rather than structurally forced.

\subsection*{Type III: irreducible postulates}
An assumption is irreducible if, even after the whole derivation is completed,
it remains a large undecomposed statement with no reduction to a finite audit.
Such a hypothesis remains a genuine postulate of the framework.

\section{2. Application to the current TECT bottlenecks}

\subsection*{(A) Microscopic branch assumption}

The working branch
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi,P]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
\]
is currently a \emph{working microscopic ansatz}.

This assumption is only partially dischargeable.
It may be weakened if one later proves one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item this branch is dynamically generated under RG from a broader UV class;
\item this branch is the minimal one compatible with the required carrier coefficients;
\item alternative branches fail to generate the same transport data.
\end{enumerate}

So this assumption is not yet naturally solved.
At present it remains a genuine branch-level postulate.

\subsection*{(B) Defect-background existence assumption}

The assumption that there exists a shell-/defect-adapted finite-energy background is much more likely to become dischargeable.

Why?
Because it can be reduced to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item radial or profile existence equations,
\item topological boundary conditions,
\item finite-energy coercivity,
\item asymptotic matching inequalities.
\end{enumerate}

So this is a good assumption:
it is large at first, but it has a clear route toward becoming a genuine existence theorem.

\subsection*{(C) Longitudinal carrier survival assumption}

This is the best example of an assumption that naturally reduces.

Initially one may say:
\[
\text{``the longitudinal carrier channel survives.''}
\]
But after the transport classification and basis reduction, this becomes
\[
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\ell_{\parallel A}=\hat n_i\hat n_jE_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
\]
This is no longer a philosophical assumption.
It is a finite basis-overlap audit.

So this assumption is not merely being postponed;
it is being \emph{compressed} into a concrete calculable statement.

\subsection*{(D) IR isotropy / Lorentz restoration assumption}

This one is intermediate.

It is not as irreducible as the branch ansatz,
because it can in principle be tested by background-field FRG, stability matrices, and anisotropy eigenvalues.
But it is not as directly dischargeable as the longitudinal carrier audit either.

So this assumption is potentially reducible, but only after a separate RG module is constructed.

\section{3. What it means for an assumption to become ``natural''}

There are two different meanings of ``natural resolution.''

\subsection*{(i) Logical naturality}
An assumption becomes logically natural if the theory shows that its failure is only possible under exact tuning.

For example, if one proves
\[
\lambda_\parallel=0
\iff
\text{exact cancellation hypersurface},
\]
then nonzero longitudinal transport is not yet a theorem from first principles,
but it becomes the generic outcome of the working branch.

\subsection*{(ii) Constructive naturality}
An assumption becomes constructively natural if it reduces to a concrete existence or computation problem.

For example,
\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\]
is constructively natural because it can be checked by explicit projected matrix elements.

\section{4. The correct strategy}

Therefore the right strategy is not to avoid assumptions altogether.
The right strategy is to admit only those assumptions that satisfy:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{forward derivation}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{explicit discharge map}.
}
\label{eq:discharge_map}
\end{equation}

In practice, each working assumption should come with one of the following tags:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Finite audit}: explicit matrix element, overlap, or coefficient extraction;
\item \textbf{Variational existence}: direct method / profile equation / asymptotic matching;
\item \textbf{Genericity}: vanishing requires exact tuning;
\item \textbf{RG completion}: requires a separate flow/stability module.
\end{enumerate}

Only such assumptions are scientifically productive.

\section{5. Honest verdict for the current project}

For the present TECT program:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the microscopic branch ansatz is still a genuine working postulate;
\item the defect-background assumption has a real chance of becoming a theorem;
\item the longitudinal carrier survival assumption is already close to being discharged, because it has reduced to a finite audit;
\item the IR isotropy/Lorentz assumption is potentially dischargeable, but only through a dedicated background-field RG analysis.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the answer is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Yes, some assumptions can later dissolve naturally, but only if they reduce to explicit audits or existence problems.}
}
\end{equation}

They do not disappear by philosophy.
They disappear only by reduction.

\section{Final summary}

A working assumption can later become naturally discharged, but only in a precise sense.

This happens when the forward derivation transforms the assumption into one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a finite matrix-element or overlap audit,
\item a variational/profile existence problem,
\item a genericity statement whose failure requires exact tuning,
\item a separate RG stability condition.
\end{enumerate}

For the present TECT program:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the microscopic branch ansatz remains a genuine working postulate;
\item the defect-background existence assumption is plausibly reducible to a theorem;
\item the longitudinal carrier-survival assumption is already close to discharge, since it has reduced to the finite condition
\[
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0;
\]
\item the IR isotropy/Lorentz assumption is potentially reducible, but only through an additional background-field RG module.
\end{enumerate}

Hence assumptions do not disappear automatically.
They become natural only when they are reduced.

The correct research rule is therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Admit only assumptions that come with an explicit discharge map.}
}
\]

\section{Three-Grade Classification of the Current Working Assumptions}

\section{Direct Gate-2 Longitudinal Closure Theorem}

At the present stage, the strongest honest theorem that can be proved directly is not yet the full unconditional numerical microscopic closure of the final projected Bloch data.
What \emph{is} already provable is the exact Gate-2 closure statement on the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch:

\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

Moreover, in the current Branch-B realization, the primitive longitudinal seed is fixed to be
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and the reduced witness coefficient is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\) is already analytically closed for the explicit defect profile, the entire longitudinal question reduces to whether the microscopic transport space contains a nonzero projection onto the primitive seed.

Thus Gate 2 is now a direct finite theorem, not an open conceptual PDE problem.

\section{1. Fixed shell-adapted longitudinal target}

Fix the shell-adapted frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\},
\]
and define the primitive longitudinal seed tensor
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\qquad
(B_\parallel)^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
(B_\parallel)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel)^2_{ij}=0.
}
\label{eq:proof_Bpar}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the dual longitudinal witness functional is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\parallel(E)=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,E^{\,3}_{ij}.
}
\label{eq:proof_Lpar}
\end{equation}

For any basis \(\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d\) of the actual microscopic transport space
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}:=L_\parallel(E_A)=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:proof_ellA}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Basis decomposition and exact audit criterion}

Let
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
be the shell seed space.
Each microscopic basis element admits the shell-adapted decomposition
\begin{equation}
E_A
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp V_{\min}.
\label{eq:proof_EA_decomp}
\end{equation}

Because \(L_\parallel\) annihilates \(B_I,B_J\) and \(R_A\), while \(L_\parallel(B_\parallel)\neq0\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}=L_\parallel(E_A)=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\mu_\parallel:=L_\parallel(B_\parallel)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:proof_lA_muA}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A:a_A\neq0.
}
\label{eq:proof_basis_a_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if \(N_{\mathrm{mic}}\) denotes the full microscopic shell-relevant transport tensor and
\begin{equation}
P_{\mathrm{seed}}N_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_\parallel
+
c_I^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_I
+
c_J^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_J,
\label{eq:proof_seed_proj}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:proof_basis_to_cpar}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite Gate-2 criterion.

\section{3. Primitive Branch-B longitudinal source}

In the exact concrete Class II Branch-B realization, the longitudinal primitive source is fixed by the defect geometry.
Indeed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:proof_T2tr}
\end{equation}
hence the canonical odd first-order longitudinal transport seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:proof_Vparallel}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced longitudinal witness is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:proof_lambda_from_c}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Nonvanishing of the overlap integral}

For the explicit reflection-symmetric defect profile
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
with the normalized low modes
\[
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\tanh(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
the primitive longitudinal overlap is
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:proof_Itheta3_eval}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:proof_Itheta3_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Direct Gate-2 closure theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Direct Gate-2 longitudinal closure]
Fix the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch and suppose the concrete longitudinal realization is on Branch B, so that
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
\]
and
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Assume \(\theta_0\kappa\neq0\).
Then the following are equivalent:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exists a microscopic basis vector \(E_A\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) such that
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0;
\]

\item the primitive longitudinal seed coefficient is nonzero:
\[
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Moreover, either condition implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:proof_G2_main}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:proof_basis_to_cpar},
\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq0.
\]
By \eqref{eq:proof_lambda_from_c},
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:proof_Itheta3_nonzero}, the overlap factor \(I_{\theta'^3}\) is nonzero whenever \(\theta_0\kappa\neq0\).
Therefore
\[
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
\]
Combining the two implications yields \eqref{eq:proof_G2_main}.
\end{proof}

\section{6. Practical one-mediator sufficient form}

Inside the finite coefficient-matching dictionary of the current Class II branch, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:proof_lambda_Lstar}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the practical Branch-B overlap form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3.
}
\label{eq:proof_lambda_practical}
\end{equation}

Hence the practical sufficient conditions
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0
}
\label{eq:proof_suff_Lstar}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0
}
\label{eq:proof_suff_practical}
\end{equation}
imply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:proof_practical_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest status}

This proves the exact direct theorem that is available \emph{now}.

What is proved:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

What is not yet proved from the currently inserted microscopic data alone is the unconditional statement
\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\]
for the final complete projected Bloch operator without any remaining finite insertion.
That still requires the actual evaluation of the projected microscopic data
\[
E_\pm(0),\qquad \mathcal U_j(0),\qquad C_\parallel
\]
or, equivalently, the explicit final insertion of \(L_*\) or \(\lambda_{c;OO}\).

\section{Final summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the primitive longitudinal channel is uniquely fixed to
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]

Its reduced witness is exactly
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

For the explicit defect profile, the overlap integral is analytically nonzero:
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq0).
\]

On the microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), the longitudinal audit is
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
\]
Using the shell-seed decomposition,
\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq0.
\]

Therefore the exact Gate-2 closure theorem is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

Equivalently, in the finite coefficient-matching form,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
or in the practical one-mediator form,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3.
\]

Hence
\[
\alpha_X\neq0,\ L_*\neq0,\ I_{\theta'^3}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\]
and equivalently
\[
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0,\ C_\parallel\neq0,\ I_3\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
\]

What remains open is no longer the theorem.
It is only the final finite insertion proving the antecedent
\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
\]
for the actual complete projected microscopic branch.

\section{Term-by-Term Longitudinal Audit of the \(OO\) Block}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the current explicit library, the orientational diagonal block is
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
\]

The longitudinal witness is extracted from the first-order tangent transport part through
\[
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)\bigr),
\]
and the shell expansion defines
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\qquad \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
\]

The direct audit shows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the kinetic Laplacian piece \(-Z_{O,k}\partial^2\) gives no first-order worldvolume transport;
\item the potential block \(\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)\) gives no first-order transport;
\item the derivative-anisotropy block \(Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}\) does not generate a nonzero Branch-A coefficient in the solved lowest-order class;
\item therefore the only genuine leading longitudinal carrier inside \(OO\) is \(\mathcal T_{OO}\).
\end{enumerate}

Hence
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
\]
and therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

So the current Gate-2 problem is reduced to the single finite question
\[
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?.
\]

\section{1. Block to be audited}

On the background-dependent Hessian, the orientational diagonal block has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
}
\label{eq:OO_block_start}
\end{equation}

The general tangent first-order shell-compatible transport operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
a_0(\xi)\,n^\mu\Pi_Q
+
a_3(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
b_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
b_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:general_tangent_block}
\end{equation}

The load-bearing longitudinal profile is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:a3_trace_extract}
\end{equation}

Restricted to the \(OO\) block, write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:hpar_OO_def}
\end{equation}

Its shell expansion defines the longitudinal coefficients:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\cdots.
}
\label{eq:hpar_OO_expand}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Why the kinetic and potential pieces do not contribute}

The term
\[
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
\]
is purely second-order in spacetime derivatives and does not generate a first-order worldvolume transport block of the form
\[
-i\,\mathcal M^\mu\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]
Hence it contributes neither to \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\) nor to \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\).

Likewise, the potential block
\[
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
\]
is multiplicative in \(\xi\) and contains no worldvolume derivative at first order.
Therefore it also gives no direct contribution to the longitudinal transport coefficients.

Thus the first two pieces of \eqref{eq:OO_block_start} are inert for the present audit.

\section{3. Why there is no Branch-A term in the solved lowest-order class}

The branch-sensitive longitudinal parametrization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:branch_sensitive_a3}
\end{equation}

Inside the solved lowest-order realization, the linear Branch-A coefficient vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:BranchA_zero}
\end{equation}

Independently, the reflection-symmetry and projector-commutator audit shows that the longitudinal monomial
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
\]
is forbidden, whereas the first allowed one is

\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\label{eq:ell1_zero_exact}
\end{equation}
exactly, and only the cubic primitive channel survives.

Consequently, the derivative-anisotropy piece
\[
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\]
does not produce a nonzero Branch-A coefficient in the current solved lowest-order class.

\section{4. The only surviving leading \(OO\)-block carrier}

After eliminating the kinetic, potential, and Branch-A-forbidden contributions, the only genuine leading longitudinal carrier inside the \(OO\) block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}.

\label{eq:TOO_only_source}
\end{equation}

\end{equation}

\section{Direct elimination of \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_{c;OO}$}{lambda c;OO} in the current Branch-B working branch}

This is a genuine advance.

It is reduced to the Bloch-calibration constant \(C_\parallel\).

\section{Direct reduction of the final longitudinal bottleneck to a symmetry-nonprotection statement}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the current one-mediator Branch-B stage, the remaining quantity \(C_\parallel\) is not an additional independent dynamical mystery.
It is exactly the normalized \(\sigma_3\)-trace of the projected longitudinal shell matrix \(M^\parallel\).

Therefore the question
\[
C_\parallel\neq 0\ ?
\]
is equivalent to
\[
\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\neq 0
\]
provided \(\alpha_X\beta_X\neq 0\) and \(I_3\neq 0\).

Since
\[
\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel)=M_{11}-M_{22},
\]
the final longitudinal obstruction is reduced to:
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\quad\text{forced or not?}
\]

If the carrier doublet \(u_1,u_2\) is split by an exact grading/parity/chirality operator \(J\), or if \(u_1,u_2\) differ by any additional exact conserved microscopic label, then no label-preserving exchange symmetry can force \(M_{11}=M_{22}\).
In that case, the vanishing of the \(\sigma_3\)-trace is only accidental fine tuning.

So the strongest honest next theorem is:
\[
\text{under an actual internal label split, }C_\parallel=0\text{ is not symmetry-protected.}
\]

\section{1. Exact definition of \texorpdfstring{$C_\parallel$}{Cparallel}}

In the one-mediator Branch-B shell audit, the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3.
}
\label{eq:Cpar_start}
\end{equation}

On the other hand, the projected shell matrix \(M^\parallel\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel).
}
\label{eq:lambda_trace_form}
\end{equation}

Equating \eqref{eq:Cpar_start} and \eqref{eq:lambda_trace_form} gives the exact normalization identity
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac{2}{I_3}
\left(
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X}
\right)
\frac12Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel).
}
\label{eq:Cpar_exact_def}
\end{equation}

Hence, whenever
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq 0,
\qquad
I_3\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:nonzero_prefactors}
\end{equation}
one has the exact equivalence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Cpar_trace_equiv}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Reduction to diagonal asymmetry}

Since \(M^\parallel\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix, under the locked longitudinal selection rule it contributes through the \(\sigma_3\)-channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\parallel
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_3\sigma_3,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel).
}
\label{eq:Mpar_sigma3}
\end{equation}

In the diagonal carrier basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
}
\label{eq:m3_diag}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
}
\label{eq:Cpar_diag_equiv}
\end{equation}

So the remaining longitudinal calibration problem is exactly the diagonal asymmetry problem.

\section{3. Non-forbiddance of the longitudinal channel}

At the shell-reduced symmetry level, the longitudinal channel is not symmetry-forbidden.
Rather, it is the unique singlet-to-singlet intertwiner
\[
p_\parallel\longleftrightarrow \sigma_3.
\]
Equivalently, in the minimal shell-allowed tensor space
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
the direction \(B_\parallel\) is allowed rather than excluded.

Thus the residual shell symmetry does not force
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}=0.
\]
So longitudinal failure cannot be blamed on the minimal shell symmetry itself.

\section{4. Exact obstruction theorem for exchange-protected equality}

Now suppose there were an exact symmetry forcing
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}.
\]
This would require an exact label-preserving exchange involution \(S\) on the carrier doublet, swapping
\[
Su_1=u_2,\qquad Su_2=u_1,
\]
while preserving the full microscopic label package.

Let \(J\) be an exact grading/parity/chirality involution.
If
\[
Ju_1=\epsilon_1u_1,\qquad Ju_2=\epsilon_2u_2,\qquad \epsilon_i\in\{\pm1\},
\]
and \(S\) preserves labels, then necessarily
\[
[S,J]=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\epsilon_1=\epsilon_2
\]
is necessary for such an exchange symmetry to exist.

Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\epsilon_1\neq \epsilon_2,
}
\label{eq:Jsplit}
\end{equation}
then no exact label-preserving exchange involution exists.

More generally, if \(u_1,u_2\) differ by any additional exact conserved microscopic label, the same obstruction holds.

Thus:

\begin{theorem}[Symmetry-nonprotection of the longitudinal diagonal asymmetry]
Assume \(\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0\) and \(I_3\neq0\).
If the reduced carrier doublet \(u_1,u_2\) satisfies either
\begin{enumerate}
\item an exact grading/parity/chirality split \(\epsilon_1\neq\epsilon_2\), or
\item a mismatch in an additional exact conserved microscopic label,
\end{enumerate}
then no exact label-preserving exchange symmetry can force
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}.
\]
Therefore the vanishing
\[
\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel)=0
\]
is not symmetry-protected.
Equivalently,
\[
C_\parallel=0
\]
can occur only by accidental fine tuning, not by exact structural necessity.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under either hypothesis, an exact exchange involution preserving the full label package does not exist.
Hence the equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is not enforced by exact symmetry.
But by \eqref{eq:m3_diag},
\[
\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel)=M_{11}-M_{22}.
\]
Therefore its vanishing is accidental rather than symmetry-protected.
By \eqref{eq:Cpar_trace_equiv}, the same conclusion holds for \(C_\parallel\).
\end{proof}

\section{5. Strongest honest generic conclusion}

The previous theorem does not yet compute the actual numerical value of \(C_\parallel\).
But it gives the strongest honest generic statement currently available:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{if the carrier doublet is actually label-split, then }C_\parallel=0\text{ is nongeneric.}
}
\label{eq:Cpar_nongeneric_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence, under the same hypotheses and away from accidental fine tuning,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Cpar_generic_yes}
\end{equation}

\section{6. What is still not unconditional}

What is not yet proved from the currently inserted microscopic data alone is the unconditional statement
\[
C_\parallel\neq0
\]
for the final complete refined locked Bloch operator.

The remaining fork is exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either verify an actual internal }J\text{-split between }u_1,u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\label{eq:last_fork}
\end{equation}

If the split is verified, then zero is not symmetry-protected.
If not, one must evaluate the projected diagonal asymmetry directly.

\section{Final summary}

The remaining longitudinal calibration constant is not an independent mystery.
It is exactly the normalized \(\sigma_3\)-trace of the projected longitudinal shell matrix:
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac{2}{I_3}

\[

\qquad
I_3\neq0,

\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq0
\iff
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\neq0
\iff
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
}

At the shell-reduced symmetry level, the longitudinal channel is not symmetry-forbidden.
It is the unique singlet-to-singlet intertwiner

p_\parallel\longleftrightarrow \sigma_3.
\]

Therefore vanishing of \(C_\parallel\) cannot be attributed to the minimal shell symmetry.

Moreover, if the carrier doublet \(u_1,u_2\) is split by an exact grading/parity/chirality operator \(J\), or differs by any additional exact conserved microscopic label, then no label-preserving exchange involution can force
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}.
\]
Hence
\[

\]
is not symmetry-protected and can occur only by accidental fine tuning.

Under the first outcome, the generic conclusion is

\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.

\section{What the actual \(J\)-grading does and does not prove}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The uploaded documents do contain an actual exact grading \(J\), but it is a \(2+2\) reflection grading,
not yet an internal split of the carrier doublet itself.

Concretely, the low-energy modes are
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\]
with reflection
\[
(Ju)(\xi)=u(-\xi),
\qquad
Ju_a^\pm=\pm u_a^\pm.
\]

Therefore the grading proves:
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\Pi_\pm \mathcal D_1 \Pi_\pm =0,
\]
so the leading reduced operator is block-off-diagonal.

However, this does \emph{not} yet imply an internal label split between the two basis vectors inside a fixed
two-dimensional carrier block.
Indeed, \(u_1^+,u_2^+\) have the same \(J\)-eigenvalue, and \(u_1^-,u_2^-\) have the same \(J\)-eigenvalue.

Hence the currently verified grading does not by itself force
\[
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
\]

So the final longitudinal problem is no longer:
\[
\text{``is there an exact grading?''}
\]
That is already answered positively.

It is now:
\[
\boxed{
(\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)_{22}\neq0\ ?
}
\]
namely the direct projected diagonal-asymmetry computation.

\section{Final summary}

The uploaded documents do contain an actual exact grading \(J\), but it is a reflection-based \(2+2\) grading:
\[
Ju_a^\pm=\pm u_a^\pm,
\qquad
\mathcal K_+=\mathrm{span}\{u_1^+,u_2^+\},
\qquad
\mathcal K_-=\mathrm{span}\{u_1^-,u_2^-\}.
\]

This is sufficient to prove the block-off-diagonal form of the leading reduced operator:
\[
\Pi_\pm \mathcal D_1 \Pi_\pm = 0.
\]

However, it is not an internal split of the carrier doublet within a fixed \(2\times2\) block.
Therefore it does not by itself force the diagonal asymmetry
\[
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
\]

So the final longitudinal bottleneck is no longer the existence of a grading.
That part is already closed.

The remaining problem is the direct projected diagonal-asymmetry computation:
\[
\boxed{
(\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)_{22}\neq0,
}
\]
where
\[
(W_+)_i{}_{ab}
=
\left\langle +G_*,e_a\middle|
\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(0)
\middle|+G_*,e_b\right\rangle.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12Tr(\sigma_3\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)
=
\frac12\Bigl[(\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\cdot \vec W_+)_{22}\Bigr].
\]

Thus the remaining longitudinal task is a direct projected matrix-element calculation, not a further structural theorem.

\section{Corrected longitudinal extraction formulas without raw \texorpdfstring{$\backslash$Tr}{\Tr}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

From now on, every trace is written as \(\operatorname{Tr}\), not \(\Tr\).
Moreover, for the longitudinal coefficient, the trace formula can be replaced completely by the diagonal-difference formula, which is safer and more explicit.

The exact projected extraction formula is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr),
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_i K_i.
\]

Equivalently, in the \(2\times2\) \(+\)-valley core basis,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Bigl[(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}\Bigr].
\]

This second formula avoids any trace notation and is the best one to use for the remaining direct computation.

\section{1. Corrected exact extraction formulas}

The shell-projected microscopic derivative data are
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
\left.\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
M_i=P_*K_iP_*.
\label{eq:K_M_def_correct}
\end{equation}
The exact coefficient extraction formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 M_\parallel\bigr),
\qquad
M_\parallel:=\hat n_i M_i,
}
\label{eq:lambda_trace_correct}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma_1 M_1\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma_2 M_1\bigr).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_trace_correct}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if one uses the projected \(+\)-valley derivative block
\begin{equation}
(W_+)_i{}_{ab}
:=
\left\langle +G_*,e_a\middle|
\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(0)
\middle|+G_*,e_b\right\rangle,
\qquad a,b=1,2,
\label{eq:Wp_def_correct}
\end{equation}
then the longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Bigl[(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:lambda_diagdiff_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus the remaining longitudinal test is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:last_longitudinal_test}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact Schur-complement derivative formula}

The current working branch uses
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}(k).
\label{eq:Heff_schur_again}
\end{equation}
Differentiating with respect to \(k_\parallel:=\hat n_i k_i\) gives
\begin{align}
K_\parallel
&:=
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
\nonumber\\
&=
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
-
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\Psi X}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}\,H_{XX}^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-
H_{\Psi X}\,H_{XX}^{-1}\,\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{X\Psi}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
+
H_{\Psi X}\,H_{XX}^{-1}\,
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{XX}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}\,
H_{XX}^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}.
\label{eq:Kpar_schur_general}
\end{align}

In the present minimal Class II truncation,
\begin{equation}
H_{XX}=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X,
\qquad
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{XX}=0,
\label{eq:HXX_constant}
\end{equation}
so this simplifies exactly to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel
=
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\Psi\Psi}\big|_{k_*}
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\bigl(\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\Psi X}\bigr)\big|_{k_*}\,H_{X\Psi}
+
H_{\Psi X}\,\bigl(\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{X\Psi}\bigr)\big|_{k_*}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Kpar_schur_reduced}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact diagonal-difference decomposition}

Projecting \eqref{eq:Kpar_schur_reduced} to the \(+\)-valley internal basis gives
\begin{equation}
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{aa}
=
D^{(0)}_a-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_a,
\qquad a=1,2,
\label{eq:diag_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D^{(0)}_a
:=
\left\langle +G_*,e_a\middle|
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\Psi\Psi}\big|_{k_*}
\middle|+G_*,e_a\right\rangle,
\label{eq:D0_def}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
D^{(\mathrm{med})}_a
:=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left\langle +G_*,e_a\middle|
\bigl(\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\Psi X}\bigr)\big|_{k_*}\,H_{X\Psi}
+
H_{\Psi X}\,\bigl(\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{X\Psi}\bigr)\big|_{k_*}
\middle|+G_*,e_a\right\rangle.
\label{eq:Dmed_def}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\lambda_\parallel
=
\Bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\Bigr)
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:lambda_diag_split_final}
\end{equation}

This is the exact term-by-term longitudinal formula in the current working branch.

\section{4. Correct formula for \texorpdfstring{$C_\parallel$}{Cparallel} without trace notation}

The Branch-B reduced coefficient also satisfies
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3,
\label{eq:lambda_Cpar_branchB_again}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
I_3=I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:I3_again}
\end{equation}

Combining \eqref{eq:lambda_diagdiff_exact} and \eqref{eq:lambda_Cpar_branchB_again} yields the exact calibration identity
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X\,I_3}
\Bigl[
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Cpar_diagdiff_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore, provided
\[
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq 0,
\qquad
I_3\neq 0,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
\neq
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}
\label{eq:Cpar_nonzero_diagdiff}
\end{equation}

\section{5. What remains to be computed}

The final longitudinal task is no longer to discuss abstract traces or structural channels.

It is exactly the direct projected matrix-element computation of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}
\label{eq:final_compute_target}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using \eqref{eq:lambda_diag_split_final}, one may compute
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\Bigr)
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:final_compute_target_split}
\end{equation}

This is the safest exact formula to use going forward.

\section{Final summary}

The raw command \verb|\Tr| is not used anymore.
All trace formulas are written with \(\operatorname{Tr}\), and whenever possible the trace is replaced by an explicit diagonal-difference formula.

The corrected longitudinal extraction formulas are
\[
\lambda_\parallel

\qquad

\Bigr].
}
\]

Hence
\[
2\lambda_\parallel
=
\Bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\Bigr)
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr),
\]
with

+
H_{\Psi X}(\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{X\Psi})
|+G_*,e_a\rangle.
\]

The exact calibration identity is
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=

\Bigl[

-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\]

Therefore the final longitudinal task is exactly the direct projected matrix-element computation of

-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}

\section{Direct compression of the longitudinal audit to the pure \(JJ\)-sector}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the longitudinal primitive channel is no longer a broad projected-derivative mystery.

The uploaded branch-level source-classification theorem shows that, at principal shell order,

\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure \(K\)-sector has no leading longitudinal component,
\item the mixed \(JK\)-sector generates transverse Pauli directions only,
\item the \(KK\)-sector remains in the transverse family at principal longitudinal shell order,
\item therefore the primitive longitudinal coefficient is localized entirely to the pure \(JJ\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the longitudinal problem is reduced to a single coefficient:
\[
\lambda_c^{(JJ)} \neq 0,
\]
or equivalently to the axial shell-singlet amplitude \(j^2\neq 0\).

\section{1. Starting point: Schur-complement channel split}

In the current Class II branch, the shell-relevant witness coefficients are extracted from the Schur-complement correction
\begin{equation}
\Delta_X
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)^\dagger.
\label{eq:JJ_start_schur}
\end{equation}
Therefore the physical shell channels split as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ,\qquad JK,\qquad KK.
}
\label{eq:JJJKKK_split}
\end{equation}
This is the correct post-Schur bookkeeping layer, rather than the pre-Schur tensor
\[
\alpha_X\mathsf J+\beta_X\mathsf K.
\]

\section{2. Shell-adapted leading ansatz}

Fix the shell frame
\[
(\hat n,e_1,e_2),
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and the tangent Pauli basis
\[
(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3).
\]

At the current explicit leading shell level, the \(J\)-sector is purely axial:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{a}
+
\mathsf J^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
}
\label{eq:J_leading_final}
\end{equation}
where the null part is orthogonal to the shell witness projectors.

Likewise, the \(K\)-sector is purely transverse:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^a
\Big[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r{}^{a}
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r{}^{a}
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:K_leading_final}
\end{equation}

Thus, at principal shell level, \(J\) carries the longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet direction and \(K\) carries only the transverse \(\Sigma_{1,2}\) directions.

\section{3. Longitudinal source classification}

The uploaded theorem states that, in the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the shell-relevant primitive odd longitudinal singlet \(n^\mu\Sigma_3\) can be generated only by the pure \(JJ\)-type sector at principal order.

Equivalently:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure \(K\)-sector has no leading longitudinal component,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0;
}
\label{eq:cparK_zero_again}
\end{equation}

\item the mixed \(JK\)-sector generates transverse Pauli directions only;

\item the \(KK\)-sector remains in the transverse family at principal longitudinal shell order;

\item therefore the microscopic longitudinal coefficient is localized to the \(JJ\)-sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\lambda_c^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:lambdac_JJ_only}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

So the longitudinal carrier-side frontier is no longer a general \(K_\parallel\)-audit.
It is the single finite check
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:JJ_only_test}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Explicit branch dictionary}

The current explicit branch dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2,
}
\label{eq:lambda_JJ_dictionary}
\end{equation}
while the transverse coefficients are

\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,

Hence the longitudinal/transverse split is completely sharp:

JJ \leadsto \lambda_\parallel,

The primitive longitudinal witness is therefore

\lambda_c^{(JJ)}

\section{Final summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the longitudinal primitive shell channel is localized entirely to the pure \(JJ\)-sector at principal shell order.

More precisely:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure \(K\)-sector has no leading longitudinal component,
\[
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0;
\]
\item the mixed \(JK\)-sector generates transverse Pauli directions only;
\item the \(KK\)-sector remains in the transverse family at principal longitudinal shell order;
\item therefore
\[
\lambda_c=\lambda_c^{(JJ)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The explicit current branch dictionary is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}.
}
\]

Hence the longitudinal/transverse split is sharp:
\[
JJ \leadsto \lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
JK/KK \leadsto (\alpha,\beta).
\]

Since
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0
\quad\text{for}\quad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
\]
the longitudinal nonvanishing problem is reduced to the single check
\[
\boxed{
j^2\neq0.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

So the remaining longitudinal frontier is no longer a broad projected-matrix audit.
It is the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of the axial shell-singlet coefficient \(j^2\) in the actual refined locked basis.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct projector-contraction formula for the axial shell-singlet coefficient \texorpdfstring{$j^2$}{j2}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working-branch level, the longitudinal primitive coefficient is localized entirely to the pure \(JJ\)-sector.
Therefore the only remaining longitudinal computation is the extraction of the axial shell-singlet scalar \(j^2\).

The correct way to write this is not as a broad matrix audit, but as a quadratic projector contraction on the shell-normal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet channel.

\section{1. Source localization to the pure \(JJ\)-sector}

The current branch-level source classification is:

\begin{equation}
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0
\quad
\text{at principal longitudinal shell order},
\label{eq:j2_nonJJ_zero}
\end{equation}
whereas
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\ \text{is allowed and is the unique principal Class-II longitudinal source.}
\label{eq:j2_JJ_unique}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\lambda_c^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:j2_lambdac_JJ}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Axial shell form of the \(J\)-sector}

At the same principal shell level, the axial \(J\)-sector takes the shell-normal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
J^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
}
\label{eq:j2_J_axial}
\end{equation}
where the null part is orthogonal to the shell witness projector by construction.

Thus the only shell-relevant \(J\)-data for the longitudinal channel are the coefficients \(j^a\).

\section{3. Canonical quadratic longitudinal projector}

Define the quadratic shell-longitudinal projector by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{\parallel}^{(JJ)}[X,Y]
:=
\frac12\,\delta_{ab}\,\hat n^i\hat n^{i'}\,
(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{r'}\,
X_{i,r}^{a}\,
\overline{Y_{i',}{}^{b r'}}.
}
\label{eq:j2_proj_def}
\end{equation}

This is the unique shell-normal singlet projector because it contracts:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the two spatial indices onto the shell normal \(\hat n_i\hat n_{i'}\),
\item the tangent Pauli slot onto \(\Sigma_3\),
\item the internal mediator labels with \(\delta_{ab}\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the axial shell-singlet coefficient is defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j^2
:=
\Pi_{\parallel}^{(JJ)}[J,J].
}
\label{eq:j2_def}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Evaluation on the axial shell form}

Substituting \eqref{eq:j2_J_axial} into \eqref{eq:j2_def}, and using orthogonality of the null part, gives
\begin{align}
j^2
&=
\frac12\,\delta_{ab}\,\hat n^i\hat n^{i'}(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{r'}
\Bigl(\hat n_i j^a (\Sigma_3)_r\Bigr)
\overline{\Bigl(\hat n_{i'} j^b (\Sigma_3)^{r'}\Bigr)}
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12\,(\hat n^i\hat n_i)(\hat n^{i'}\hat n_{i'})\,
\delta_{ab}\,j^a\overline{j^b}\,
(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{r'}(\Sigma_3)_{r}{}^{r'}.
\label{eq:j2_eval_raw}
\end{align}

Since \(\hat n^i\hat n_i=1\) and
\begin{equation}
(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{r'}(\Sigma_3)_{r}{}^{r'}=2,
\label{eq:j2_sigma_norm}
\end{equation}
the normalization in \eqref{eq:j2_proj_def} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j^2=\delta_{ab}\,j^a\overline{j^b}.
}
\label{eq:j2_norm_final}
\end{equation}

Thus \(j^2\) is literally the squared magnitude of the axial shell-singlet \(J\)-coefficient vector.

\section{5. Direct longitudinal dictionary}

The current explicit branch dictionary states
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,I_{\theta'^3}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
j^2.
}
\label{eq:j2_lambda_dictionary}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2.
}
\label{eq:j2_lambdac_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Hence the longitudinal primitive coefficient is completely determined by the single positive shell-singlet contraction \(j^2\).

\section{6. Immediate nonvanishing criterion}

For the explicit admissible defect profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:j2_Itheta3}
\end{equation}
Therefore, whenever \(\theta_0\kappa\neq0\),
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0.
\]

Combining this with \eqref{eq:j2_lambda_dictionary}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
j^2\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:j2_nonzero_criterion}
\end{equation}

Thus the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is exactly the verification of
\[
j^2\neq0.
\]

\section{7. What is actually still open}

The formula \eqref{eq:j2_norm_final} is exact at the present shell-reduced working-branch level.
What is not yet inserted is the actual refined-locked microscopic value of the coefficients \(j^a\).

So the remaining longitudinal computation is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the actual shell-relevant axial coefficients }j^a
\text{ in the refined locked basis and form }
j^2=\delta_{ab}j^a\overline{j^b}.
}
\label{eq:j2_actual_remaining}
\end{equation}

This is no longer a broad conceptual problem.
It is a finite coefficient extraction from the actual \(J\)-kernel.

\section{Final summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the primitive longitudinal shell singlet is sourced only by the pure \(JJ\)-sector at principal shell order:
\[
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\ \text{allowed}.
\]

The shell-relevant axial \(J\)-sector has the canonical form
\[
J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
J_{i,r}^{a,\mathrm{null}}.
\]

The correct quadratic shell-longitudinal projector is
\[
\Pi_{\parallel}^{(JJ)}[X,Y]
=
\frac12\,\delta_{ab}\,\hat n^i\hat n^{i'}(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{r'}X_{i,r}^{a}\overline{Y_{i',}{}^{b r'}}.
\]

Applying it to the \(J\)-sector defines the axial shell-singlet coefficient
\[
\boxed{
j^2:=\Pi_{\parallel}^{(JJ)}[J,J]
=
\delta_{ab}j^a\overline{j^b}.
}
\]

Therefore the current branch dictionary becomes
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2.
}
\]

Since
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq0
\quad\text{for}\quad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
\]
the nonvanishing criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
j^2\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

So the remaining longitudinal frontier is exactly the explicit evaluation of the shell-relevant axial coefficients \(j^a\), equivalently the scalar \(j^2\), in the actual refined locked basis.

\section{Final scalar reduction of the pure \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} longitudinal ingredient}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A correction is needed.

The most accurate final microscopic scalar for the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal channel is not best written as a generic \(j^2\) anymore.
In the latest refined locked/Class-II reduction, the principal \(JJ\) axial coefficient tensor collapses to a single scalar
\[
\Xi_{JJ},
\]
and this scalar is then identified with the invariant
\[
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel
\]
up to a fixed normalization factor.

So the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is more precisely
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\]
rather than a broad unresolved tensor audit.

\section{1. Collapse of the pure-\(JJ\) tensor to one scalar}

The current refined locked \(+\) Class II reduction implies that the principal pure-\(JJ\) axial coefficient tensor has the isotropic shell form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{jm}^{(JJ)}=\Xi_{JJ}\,\delta_{jm}.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_tensor}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*=\Xi_{JJ}|G_*|.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_shell_contraction}
\end{equation}

So the second microscopic longitudinal ingredient is not a rank-two tensor anymore.
It is reduced to the single scalar test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_scalar_test}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Canonical locked basis}

Fix the canonical locked basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0=(1,0,0)^T,
\qquad
u_1=(0,1,0)^T,
\qquad
u_2=(0,0,1)^T.
}
\label{eq:canonical_locked_basis}
\end{equation}

In this basis the tangent Pauli frame is fixed canonically, and the longitudinal \(JJ\) scalar can be expressed in terms of two shell-relevant invariants:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the background singlet alignment
\[
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
\]
\item the shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_def_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Identification of \texorpdfstring{$\Xi_{JJ}$}{XiJJ} with \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{Lstar}}

In the current minimal explicit Class II split, the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal scalar is not an independent new object.
It is exactly the invariant \(L_*\) up to a fixed normalization:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}=\mathcal N_{JJ}\,L_*,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_equals_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Therefore the second microscopic longitudinal ingredient is reduced from a tensor problem to a single invariant product.

\section{4. Immediate Fourier consequence}

Previously one had
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i\,\Xi_{JJ}\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
\label{eq:AhatJJ_old}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:XiJJ_equals_Lstar},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i\,\mathcal N_{JJ}\,L_*\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:AhatJJ_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
}
\label{eq:Lstar_practical}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:VparJJ_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Longitudinal closure chain}

Once the first-shell dominant carrier asymmetry condition
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq0
\]
also holds, the longitudinal chain becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0
\Longrightarrow
m_3\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:long_chain_final}
\end{equation}

So the last carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced completely to the two scalar checks
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:last_two_scalars}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Explicit extraction formulas for the two scalars}

The first scalar is the valley Bloch asymmetry
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:Delta00_final_again}
\end{equation}

The second scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:Lstar_again}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
}
\label{eq:mpar_again}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr)
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:upar_final_again}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Lstar_diag_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest status}

What is now genuinely closed is the reduction:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal ingredient is no longer a tensor problem;
\item it is one scalar \(\Xi_{JJ}\);
\item this scalar is exactly the invariant \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\) up to normalization;
\item therefore the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the pair
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet explicitly inserted is the actual refined-locked numerical or symbolic evaluation of
\[
\Delta_{00},\qquad
m_\parallel,\qquad
u_\parallel.
\]

So the remaining work is a finite scalar extraction problem, not a conceptual source-classification problem.

\section{Final summary}

A correction is required for the final pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal scalar language.

The most accurate current reduction is not best expressed solely in terms of a generic \(j^2\).
Instead, the principal pure-\(JJ\) axial coefficient tensor collapses to the scalar
\[
\boxed{
C_{jm}^{(JJ)}=\Xi_{JJ}\delta_{jm},
}

and this scalar is then identified, in the canonical locked basis, with the invariant
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}=\mathcal N_{JJ}L_*,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\]

Hence the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the two scalar checks
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

The explicit formulas are:

\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\]
\[
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
\]
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr],
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-

\Bigr].
}
\]

If
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,

then
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
m_3\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
\]

So the remaining longitudinal task is the explicit scalar extraction of
\[
\Delta_{00},\qquad m_\parallel,\qquad u_\parallel.
