\section{Direct extraction of \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel$}{L*=m_parallel u_parallel} from the canonical \(J\)-kernel}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, the longitudinal carrier test is already reduced to two finite scalars:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

The first is the valley Bloch asymmetry extracted from the two valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\).
The second is the shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias multiplied by the background selector.

The key new point is that the canonical shell form of the \(J\)-kernel already shows exactly how \(u_\parallel\) is extracted:
the shell-normal projection selects the \(\Sigma_3\) coefficient and kills the transverse \(\Sigma_{1,2}\) pieces.

\section{1. Canonical shell form of the \(J\)-kernel}

In the refined locked basis, the shell-relevant \(J\)-harmonic coefficient has the canonical form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}\,i(G_*)_i A_{G_*}
\Big[
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\Sigma_3
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)
\Big]_r{}^{b}.
}
\label{eq:J_canonical_shell}
\end{equation}

Thus the shell-normal direction \(\hat n_j\) coupled to the Pauli singlet \(\Sigma_3\) is controlled by a single scalar:
\[
u_\parallel.
\]

\section{2. Reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix}

Define the reduced intervalley matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad a,b=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Uj_def_exec}
\end{equation}

Projecting \eqref{eq:J_canonical_shell} onto the shell-normal direction gives
\begin{equation}
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
u_\parallel\,\Sigma_3
+
u_E\,(\hat n^j e_{1j}\Sigma_1+\hat n^j e_{2j}\Sigma_2)
+
u_O\,(-\hat n^j e_{2j}\Sigma_1+\hat n^j e_{1j}\Sigma_2).
\label{eq:Uj_normal_projection}
\end{equation}

Since the shell frame is orthonormal,
\[
\hat n^j e_{1j}=0,
\qquad
\hat n^j e_{2j}=0,
\]
the transverse pieces vanish and one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)=u_\parallel\,\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Uj_normal_pure}
\end{equation}

Therefore the shell-normal projected \(J\)-block is purely diagonal in the Pauli basis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_\parallel & 0\\
0 & -u_\parallel
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Uj_diag_form}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact extraction formula for \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

From \eqref{eq:Uj_diag_form}, the most robust formula is the diagonal-difference form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Big[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Big].
}
\label{eq:upar_diag_exec}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:upar_trace_exec}
\end{equation}

Thus \(u_\parallel\) is literally the diagonal asymmetry of the shell-normal projected \(J\)-block.

\section{4. Exact extraction formula for \texorpdfstring{$m_\parallel$}{m_parallel}}

In the canonical locked frame,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}.
}
\label{eq:mpar_selector_exec}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:mpar_exec}
\end{equation}

No further reduction is needed:
it is simply the \(a=3\) component of the background-current selector.

\section{5. Final scalar invariant}

Combining \eqref{eq:upar_diag_exec} and \eqref{eq:mpar_exec}, the unresolved longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Big[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Big].
}
\label{eq:Lstar_exec}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_trace_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{6. The other scalar: \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

The valley Bloch asymmetry is extracted from the low eigenvectors of the two valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\):
\begin{equation}
E_+(0)\eta_+=\varepsilon_+\eta_+,
\qquad
E_-(0)\eta_-=\varepsilon_-\eta_-,
\qquad
\eta_\pm=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(\pm)}\\
A_2^{(\pm)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:eta_pm_exec}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:Delta00_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Final longitudinal witness formula}

The current canonical branch dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_exec_final}
\end{equation}

The defect overlap is already known explicitly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:I3_exec}
\end{equation}

Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
}
\label{eq:scalar_nonzero_package}
\end{equation}
then the dominant first-shell longitudinal witness survives and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_nonzero_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest remaining computation}

So the remaining carrier-side longitudinal work is now exactly the following finite scalar extraction:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the two \(2\times2\) valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\) and diagonalize them to obtain \(\eta_\pm\), hence \(\Delta_{00}\);
\item compute the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix \(\mathcal U_j(0)\);
\item read
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Big[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Big];
\]
\item read \(m_\parallel=m^3(P_0)\);
\item form
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]
\end{enumerate}

No structural ambiguity remains.
Only these finite matrix elements remain to be inserted.

\section{Final summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to two finite scalars:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

The canonical shell form of the \(J\)-kernel already shows how \(u_\parallel\) is extracted.
After shell-normal projection, the transverse \(\Sigma_{1,2}\) components vanish by orthogonality of the shell frame, leaving only the \(\Sigma_3\) coefficient:
\[
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)=u_\parallel\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Big[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Big].
}
\]

In the canonical locked frame,
\[
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\]

Hence the final longitudinal scalar is
\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Big[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Big].
}
\]

The other scalar is the valley Bloch asymmetry
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
}
\]
where \(\eta_\pm\) are the normalized low eigenvectors of the two valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\).

The current branch dictionary is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

Thus, if
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

So the remaining longitudinal task is the literal finite extraction of
\[
E_\pm(0),\qquad \mathcal U_j(0),\qquad m^3(P_0).
\]

\section{Actual Microscopic Coefficient-Extraction Pipeline from the Bloch Operator}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The purpose of this section is not to claim that the full microscopic coefficients have already been numerically evaluated.
Rather, its role is to state the exact executable pipeline that connects the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch to the finite projected extraction of the reduced Dirac/Weyl coefficients.

\section{1. Explicit working microscopic branch}

We fix the strongest explicit microscopic working branch currently available:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:Lmic_final_exec}
\end{equation}

Here this is not claimed to be the unique final complete TECT action.
It is the current explicit working branch on which the Bloch/Hessian extraction can be carried out concretely.

\section{2. Locked 12-mode BCC background}

The periodic locked background is defined by the first reciprocal shell \(\mathcal S_{12}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:BCC12_exec}
\end{equation}

This fixes the folded Bragg shell on which the low carrier extraction is performed.

\section{3. Quadratic Bloch Hessian and exact Schur complement at quadratic level}

Linearizing the equations of motion around the periodic background yields the quadratic Bloch fiber operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Hbloch_exec}
\end{equation}

At the quadratic Bloch-Hessian level, eliminating the heavy mediator is exact and gives the Schur complement
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:Heff_schur_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Folded Bragg convention, shell projection, and low-slot projector}

We work at the folded Bragg point
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p.
}
\label{eq:folded_bragg_exec}
\end{equation}

The shell-projected operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:Hshell_exec}
\end{equation}
and the low-slot projector is spectrally defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0))^{-1}\,dz.
}
\label{eq:Pstar_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Projected derivative transport matrices}

The first-order derivative blocks are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
=
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
M_i=P_*K_iP_*.
}
\label{eq:KiMi_exec}
\end{equation}

In the adapted shell frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel=\hat n_iM_i,
\qquad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
}
\label{eq:Mframe_exec}
\end{equation}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule, the reduced coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M_\parallel),

\label{eq:lambda_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\qquad
\beta=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Calibration layer versus overlap layer}

At the Bloch-projected level, the exact normalization layer is
\begin{equation}

\qquad

\label{eq:overlap_layer_exec}

Therefore the projected derivative computation determines

directly, while the extraction of
\[

still requires the explicit normalization constants
\[
C_\parallel,\ C_E,\ C_O.

\section{7. Honest status}

\section*{Final Summary: Honest Status of the Explicit Extraction Pipeline}

\section{Gate 4 Residual Mass Audit on the Corrected Doubled Shell Block}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Once the isolated doubled local Dirac block exists, Gate 4 is a finite constant-operator audit.
It is no longer a PDE problem.

The exact constant Dirac-mass space is
\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
\]
Therefore the exact pass/fail criterion is
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]

What can be proved directly now is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) is sufficient for Gate 4;
\item even the weaker exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already sufficient;
\item Class II is compatible with mass protection, but does not by itself prove it.
\end{enumerate}

So the only remaining open microscopic question is whether the corrected isolated shell block actually preserves one of these residual valley symmetries.

\section{1. Fixed doubled Dirac block and exact mass space}

Assume the local doubled shell block has already been reduced to the anisotropic massless Dirac form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(p)
=
v_1 p_1\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_1)
+
v_2 p_2\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_2)
+
v_3 p_3\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_3).
}
\label{eq:G4_HD}
\end{equation}

The exact constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\left\{
K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):
\{K,\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i\}=0
\ \forall i=1,2,3
\right\}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_MD}
\end{equation}

Hence any constant Dirac mass has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_m
=
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:G4_general_mass}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact Gate-4 criterion}

Let \(G_{\mathrm{res}}\) be the exact residual symmetry group of the corrected isolated doubled shell block.
Define the residual constant algebra
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_Ares}
\end{equation}

Then the exact Gate-4 pass/fail criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_exact_criterion}
\end{equation}

So Gate 4 is a finite constant-operator classification problem.

\section{3. Why little-group scalarity and opposite-valley matching are not enough}

The full little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operator space on the doubled block is
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:G4_scalar_const_space}
\end{equation}

Thus little-group scalarity alone still allows both mass generators
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
So it is not enough for mass protection.

Likewise, opposite-valley matching fixes the doubled structure but does not remove the constant mass operators.
Therefore neither little-group scalarity alone nor opposite-valley matching alone implies Gate 4.

\section{4. Exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) is sufficient}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_V/2}.
}
\label{eq:G4_QV}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0,
\]
the doubled kinetic block is valley symmetric.

Now act on the two mass generators:
\begin{align}
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
&=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:G4_rot1}
\\
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
&=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:G4_rot2}
\end{align}

Thus \(\mathcal M_D\) transforms as a nontrivial charged doublet under \(U(1)_V\).
No nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_D\) is invariant under the full \(U(1)_V\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_U1_forbid}
\end{equation}

So exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) is sufficient for Gate 4.

\section{5. Exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already sufficient}

Even the weaker discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4
}
\label{eq:G4_Z2_gen}
\end{equation}
already suffices.

Indeed,
\begin{align}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
&=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:G4_Z2_mass1}
\\
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
&=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:G4_Z2_mass2}
\end{align}

Hence both mass generators are odd under \(S_V\), so no nonzero mass is invariant.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_Z2_forbid}
\end{equation}

Thus exact residual valley \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already sufficient for Gate 4.

\section{6. Class II compatibility and honest limitation}

The current Class II correction is gradient-linear and renormalizes the shell derivative coefficients, but does not by itself provide a proof that the corrected constant \(4\times4\) block preserves the required residual valley symmetry.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with mass protection, but is not by itself a proof of it.}
}
\label{eq:G4_ClassII_compatible}
\end{equation}

So the remaining microscopic question is not the classification theorem.
It is only the actual residual-symmetry audit of the corrected isolated shell block.

\section{7. Final practical Gate-4 checklist}

Gate 4 now has the following exact execution order:

\begin{enumerate}
\item identify the isolated doubled shell block and the exact mass space \(\mathcal M_D\);
\item test whether exact residual \(U(1)_V\) survives;
\item if not, test whether exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) survives;
\item if neither is manifest, compute the full residual constant algebra \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\);
\item check whether
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the theorem-level reduction of Gate 4 is complete.

\section{8. Full practical acceptance attachment}

Combining this with the carrier-side Gate 2--3 conclusion, the current branch is accepted at practical level if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G234_full_accept}
\end{equation}

This is the final practical accept/reject criterion at the carrier level.

\section{Final summary}

For the doubled local Dirac block
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\]
the exact constant Dirac-mass space is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\]

Hence the exact Gate-4 pass/fail criterion is
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
}
\]

Little-group scalarity alone is insufficient, and opposite-valley matching alone is also insufficient.

A sufficient protecting mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry:
\[
\boxed{
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\]
and even the weaker remnant
\[
\boxed{
S_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]

Therefore the theorem-level reduction of Gate 4 is complete.

The only remaining microscopic task is to determine whether the corrected isolated doubled shell block actually preserves exact residual \(U(1)_V\) or at least exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual \texorpdfstring{$Q_*$}{Q*}-Invariant Constant-Sector Audit}

\section{1. Actual canonical shell block and actual mass space}

At the actual canonical shell level, the projected massless block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2.
}
\label{eq:Qstar_Hcore}
\end{equation}

The exact residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\label{eq:Qstar_def}
\end{equation}
and the actual constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:Mactual_def}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact commutant of \texorpdfstring{$Q_*$}{Q*}}

Let
\[
\mathcal B=\{\tau_a\otimes s_b:\ a,b\in\{0,1,2,3\}\},
\qquad
\tau_0=s_0=\mathbf 1_2.
\]
For a basis element \(X_{ab}:=\tau_a\otimes s_b\),
\[
[X_{ab},Q_*]=0
\]
holds if and only if the number of factors anticomm

uting with \(\tau_3\) and \(s_3\) is even.

Indeed:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\tau_0,\tau_3\) commute with \(\tau_3\), while \(\tau_1,\tau_2\) anticommute with \(\tau_3\);
\item \(s_0,s_3\) commute with \(s_3\), while \(s_1,s_2\) anticommute with \(s_3\).
\end{itemize}

Therefore the full Hermitian commutant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:CQstar_full}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Direct exclusion of the actual mass generators}

Now test the two actual mass generators.

First,
\begin{align}
[Q_*,M_1]
&=
[\tau_3\otimes s_3,\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2]
\nonumber\\
&=
(\tau_3\tau_2-\tau_2\tau_3)\otimes s_3
\neq 0.
\label{eq:Qstar_M1_noncomm}
\end{align}

Second,
\begin{align}
[Q_*,M_2]
&=
[\tau_3\otimes s_3,\tau_1\otimes s_3]
\nonumber\\
&=
(\tau_3\tau_1-\tau_1\tau_3)\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\neq 0.
\label{eq:Qstar_M2_noncomm}
\end{align}

Hence neither \(M_1\) nor \(M_2\) belongs to \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\). Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:CQstar_cap_Mactual_zero}
\end{equation}

This is the exact algebraic core of Gate 4 in the actual basis.

\section{4. Consequence for the corrected constant sector}

Write the full corrected constant sector as
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\Sigma(0,0).
\label{eq:dHconst_split}
\end{equation}

Assume the actual corrected theory preserves the same exact residual generator \(Q_*\), namely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:Qstar_audit_assump}
\end{equation}
Then each term lies in \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\), hence
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:CQstar_cap_Mactual_zero}, we conclude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:dHconst_no_mass}
\end{equation}

Therefore no exact constant Dirac mass can appear in the corrected projected shell block.

\section{5. Shell-block-level closure and full microscopic frontier}

At shell-block level, the minimal corrected Class II block remains purely derivative and preserves the valley generator; in particular, no independent constant shell mass is inserted.
Thus the shell-block-level mass audit is already closed.

What remains microscopic is only the inheritance question:
does the same exact \(Q_*\)-symmetry survive all constant corrections and remote-sector elimination?

So the remaining yes/no test is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:last_Qstar_test}
\end{equation}

If yes, Gate 4 passes.
If no, one must isolate the explicit symmetry-breaking constant term and test whether it has a nonzero projection onto \(M_1\) or \(M_2\).

\section{6. Final actual Gate-4 theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Actual \(Q_*\)-invariant constant-sector theorem]
Assume the actual projected shell block has the canonical massless form \eqref{eq:Qstar_Hcore}, with residual generator \(Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\), and actual mass space \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) given by \eqref{eq:Mactual_def}.

If the full corrected constant sector preserves \(Q_*\), i.e. \eqref{eq:Qstar_audit_assump} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\end{equation}
Hence no exact constant Dirac mass can appear.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:Qstar_audit_assump}, each constant correction lies in \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\).
By \eqref{eq:CQstar_cap_Mactual_zero}, \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}\).
Therefore \(\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\) cannot contain any actual mass component.
\end{proof}

\section{Final summary}

In the actual canonical shell basis, the projected massless block is
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2,
\]
with residual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\]
and actual mass space
\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

The exact Hermitian commutant of \(Q_*\) is
\[
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
\]

Neither actual mass generator belongs to this commutant:
\[
[Q_*,\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2]\neq0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\tau_1\otimes s_3]\neq0.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

Hence, if the full corrected constant sector preserves the same exact \(Q_*\), namely
\[
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\]
and no exact constant Dirac mass can appear.

Thus the theorem-level mass audit is completely closed.
The only remaining microscopic yes/no input is whether the actual full corrected constant sector really preserves the same exact residual generator \(Q_*\).

\section{Explicit Derivative Formulas for \texorpdfstring{$K_i$}{Ki} in the Bloch-Operator Extraction Pipeline}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

From this point onward, we stay strictly inside the Bloch-operator extraction pipeline:
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
\to
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

The next actual calculation is therefore the explicit derivative formula for
\[
K_i:=\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}.
\]

The important point is that the effective derivative splits into exactly three pieces:
\[
\boxed{
K_i
=
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}.
}
\]
This is the first genuine operator-construction step.

\section{1. Working microscopic branch and Bloch fiber}

We fix the refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:Ki_working_branch}
\end{equation}

Linearization around the locked 12-mode BCC background yields the Bloch Hessian
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_Bloch_block}
\end{equation}

At the first mediator-elimination stage, the exact quadratic effective block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:Ki_Heff_first}
\end{equation}

At the final shell-isolation stage, including remote spectator elimination, one writes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{low,low}}(k)
-
H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(k)\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)^{-1}\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(k).
}
\label{eq:Ki_Heff_comp}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Folded-Bragg derivative definition}

Work in the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p.
}
\label{eq:Ki_folded}
\end{equation}

Then the first derivative blocks are defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
=
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_def_final}
\end{equation}

These are the objects that are later projected to the low shell slot.

\section{3. Exact derivative of the remote Schur complement}

Let
\[
A(k):=H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(k),
\qquad
R(k):=H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)^{-1},
\qquad
B(k):=H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(k).
\]
Then
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)=H_{\mathrm{low,low}}(k)-A(k)R(k)B(k).
\]

Differentiating gives
\begin{align}
K_i
&=
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{low,low}}(k)\right|_{k_*}
-
\left.\partial_{k_i}A(k)\right|_{k_*}R_*B_*
-
A_*R_*\left.\partial_{k_i}B(k)\right|_{k_*}
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
A_*R_*
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)\right|_{k_*}
R_*B_*,
\label{eq:Ki_schur_derivative}
\end{align}
where
\[
R_*:=H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k_*)^{-1},
\qquad
A_*:=A(k_*),
\qquad
B_*:=B(k_*).
\]

This is the exact derivative formula at the final remote-eliminated level.

\section{4. Bare / Class II / spectator splitting}

The documents state that each effective shell quantity splits exactly as
\[
\text{effective}=\text{bare}+\text{Class II}+\text{spectator}.
\]
Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
=
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_three_split}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(a) Bare piece}
The bare contribution comes from the periodic \(\Psi\Psi\)-block:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}
=
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{per}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_bare}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(b) Class II piece}
Define
\[
\mathcal C(k):=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]
At leading heavy-mass order,
\[
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X+O(k,\text{periodic}),
\qquad
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger+O(M_X^{-4}).
\]
Therefore the explicit derivative contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left[
\left(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C\right)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C\left(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger\right)
\right]_{k=k_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_ClassII}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(c) Spectator piece}
The spectator correction is the remote-sector derivative inherited from the second Schur complement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}
=
-
\left.\partial_{k_i}A(k)\right|_{k_*}R_*B_*
-
A_*R_*\left.\partial_{k_i}B(k)\right|_{k_*}
+
A_*R_*
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)\right|_{k_*}
R_*B_*.
}
\label{eq:Ki_spec}
\end{equation}

Thus the microscopic coefficient problem is reduced to three explicit derivative blocks.

\section{5. Shell projection and reduced coefficients}

Let \(P_*\) be the low-slot shell projector.
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_i=P_*K_iP_*.
}
\label{eq:Ki_projected}
\end{equation}

In the adapted shell frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal},
\]
define
\[
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i,
\qquad
K_1=e_{1i}K_i,
\qquad
K_2=e_{2i}K_i,
\]
and similarly
\[
M_\parallel=\hat n_iM_i,
\qquad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
\]

The exact reduced coefficient extraction formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3M_\parallel\bigr),
}
\label{eq:Ki_lambda_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^a P_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:Ki_alpha_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac14
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
-
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:Ki_beta_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{6. The four actual microscopic quantities}

The immediate finite bookkeeping target is the quartet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:Ki_four_targets}
\end{equation}

These are exactly the shell Fourier data from which the projected derivative blocks are assembled.
Equivalently, the remaining microscopic problem is to compute the explicit reciprocal-harmonic matrix elements of
\[
\mathcal J(k),\qquad \mathcal K(k),\qquad H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)
\]
at the intervalley harmonic \(Q=G_*\).

\section{7. Honest current status inside the pipeline}

The Bloch-operator extraction pipeline is structurally closed.
The next actual computation is the derivative construction
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),\ H_{\Psi X}(k),\ H_{XX}(k)
\to
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})},\ K_i^{(\mathrm{II})},\ K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

What is still not explicitly evaluated is the branch-specific harmonic data entering
\[
\mathcal J(k),\qquad
\mathcal K(k),\qquad
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k).
\]
So the pipeline is no longer conceptually open; it is an explicit derivative-and-projection computation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Folded-Bragg Shell Bookkeeping for the Four Finite Microscopic Quantities}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the Bloch-operator extraction pipeline, the infinite-dimensional microscopic problem is reduced to four finite shell quantities:
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
\]

These control, respectively,

\begin{enumerate}
\item the scalar intervalley shell offset,
\item the first transverse witness,
\item the second transverse witness,
\item the longitudinal shell slope.
\end{enumerate}

Each splits as
\[
\text{effective}=\text{bare}+\text{Class II}+\text{spectator}.
\]

Thus the next executable stage in the pipeline is to write these four objects explicitly before inserting the final branch-specific harmonic data.

\section{1. The four shell quantities}

At the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the shell-pair bookkeeping is organized by the four finite quantities
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
}
\label{eq:FBQ_M0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
}
\label{eq:FBQ_Walpha}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\frac{
E^{\mathrm{eff}}_+(E_*,p)-E^{\mathrm{eff}}_-(E_*,p)
}{2}
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_vparallel}
\end{equation}

These are exactly the shell data from which the reduced symbol is assembled.

\section{2. Effective split: bare + Class II + spectator}

Each shell quantity splits into three pieces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:FBQ_Usplit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
}
\label{eq:FBQ_Tsplit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_vsplit}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite bookkeeping format of the current pipeline.

\section{3. Reduced-coefficient dictionary}

Once the four shell quantities are known, the reduced coefficient point is fixed.

The longitudinal coefficient is read from the shell slope:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=v_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_lambda_vpar}
\end{equation}

The two transverse matrices determine the reduced pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:FBQ_ab_dict}
\end{equation}
where \(c_E,c_O\) are the shell-seed projections of
\[
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*).
\]

Equivalently, the final finite nondegeneracy criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq0
\ \text{or}\
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_finite_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Explicit Class II transverse overlap formula}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, the transverse derivative bookkeeping compresses to the single Fourier convolution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_TII_overlap}
\end{equation}

In the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\propto
iA_{G_*}\bigl(C_\alpha\!\cdot\!G_*\bigr),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_TII_firstshell}
\end{equation}

Therefore the strongest practical explicit transverse test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_TII_test}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Role of the \(K\)-sector}

At the explicit shell-adapted leading level,
\[
\mathcal K_\parallel^{a}(G_*;0)=0,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_cparK_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus the \(K\)-sector is not a direct longitudinal source at principal shell order.
Its role is transverse:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E^{(K)}\neq0\ \text{in general},
\qquad
c_O^{(K)}\neq0\ \text{in general}.
}
\label{eq:FBQ_K_transverse_role}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual transverse witnesses must come from the genuinely nontrivial \(JK\) and/or \(KK\) shell realization.

\section{6. Honest status of the four-quantity bookkeeping}

At this point, the pipeline is no longer conceptually open.

What is fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the four finite shell quantities,
\item their exact split into bare / Class II / spectator pieces,
\item the longitudinal reading through \(v_\parallel\),
\item the transverse reading through \(\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\) and \(\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\).
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the actual symbolic or numerical insertion of the final harmonic data:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat J_i^A(Q),\qquad
\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q),\qquad
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},\qquad
\text{and spectator renormalizations.}
}
\label{eq:FBQ_honest_open}
\end{equation}

\section{Final summary}

Inside the Bloch-operator extraction pipeline, the remaining microscopic problem has been reduced to four finite shell quantities:
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
\]

They split exactly as
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\widehat U_{(II)}
+
\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})},
\]
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})},
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
\]
\[
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

The reduced finite nondegeneracy test is
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq0
\ \text{or}\
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq0.
}
\]

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, the transverse Class II piece is already compressed to the Fourier convolution
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
\]

Thus the next strict pipeline step is the longitudinal column:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Concrete Formulas for the Longitudinal Column}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the folded-Bragg shell bookkeeping, the longitudinal column is controlled by the single scalar shell slope
\[
v_\parallel.
\]
The exact bookkeeping split is
\[
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

At the reduced-symbol level one also has
\[
\lambda_\parallel=v_\parallel
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Therefore the concrete longitudinal task is to write each of the three pieces
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
\]
directly from the projected Bloch derivative operator.

\section{1. Exact projected definition}

Let
\[
K_i
=
\left.\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i.
\]
Then the longitudinal shell slope is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:long_vpar_exact_trace}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the \(+\)-valley internal \(2\times2\) block,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:long_vpar_diagdiff}
\end{equation}

This is the safest exact formula for the longitudinal column.

\section{2. Bare / Class II / spectator split}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel
=
K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
K_\parallel^{(II)}
+
K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:long_Ksplit}
\end{equation}
Then, by linearity of the projection and the trace,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})},
}
\label{eq:long_vsplit_again}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{align}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}P_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:long_vbare_def}
\\
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{(II)}P_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:long_vII_def}
\\
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:long_vsp_def}
\end{align}

\section{3. Bare longitudinal piece}

The bare longitudinal piece comes from the direct periodic \(\Psi\Psi\)-block:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{per}}(p)
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:long_Kbare}
\end{equation}
Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{per}}(p)
\right|_{p=0}
P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:long_vbare_formula}
\end{equation}

If one uses the valley-diagonal shell blocks \(E_\pm^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)\), this can be written equivalently as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:long_vbare_Epm}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Class II longitudinal piece}

Let
\[
\mathcal C(k):=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]
At leading heavy-mass order,
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
\]
Therefore the Class II derivative contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel^{(II)}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left[
\bigl(\partial_{p_\parallel}\mathcal C\bigr)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C\bigl(\partial_{p_\parallel}\mathcal C^\dagger\bigr)
\right]_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:long_KII_formula}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(
\sigma^3P_*
\left[
\bigl(\partial_{p_\parallel}\mathcal C\bigr)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C\bigl(\partial_{p_\parallel}\mathcal C^\dagger\bigr)
\right]_{p=0}
P_*
\right).
}
\label{eq:long_vII_formula}
\end{equation}

At the reduced witness level, the same longitudinal coefficient is also written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:long_seed_dict}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}+c_\parallel^{(JK)}+c_\parallel^{(KK)}.
}
\label{eq:long_cpar_split}
\end{equation}
Therefore the Class II longitudinal piece may equivalently be organized by the shell-seed split
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(II)}\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(II)}
=
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}+c_\parallel^{(JK)}+c_\parallel^{(KK)}.
}
\label{eq:long_vII_seed}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Spectator longitudinal piece}

Let
\[
A(p):=H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(p),
\qquad
R(p):=H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(p)^{-1},
\qquad
B(p):=H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(p).
\]
The remote Schur complement contributes
\[
-A(p)R(p)B(p)
\]
to the shell block.
Differentiating gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
-
\left.\partial_{p_\parallel}A(p)\right|_{p=0}R_*B_*
-
A_*R_*\left.\partial_{p_\parallel}B(p)\right|_{p=0}
+
A_*R_*\left.\partial_{p_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(p)\right|_{p=0}R_*B_*,
}
\label{eq:long_Ksp_formula}
\end{equation}
where
\[
A_*=A(0),\qquad
B_*=B(0),\qquad
R_*=H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(0)^{-1}.
\]
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:long_vsp_formula}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Honest status of the longitudinal column}

The longitudinal column is therefore completely fixed at the formal level:
\[
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

What remains open is not the formula, but the actual branch-specific insertion of
\[
E_\pm^{\mathrm{bare}}(p),\qquad
\mathcal J(k),\qquad
\mathcal K(k),\qquad
H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(p),\qquad
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(p).
\]

So the next legitimate microscopic step is the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
\]
for the chosen refined locked \(+\) Class II branch.

\section{Final summary}

The longitudinal column in the Bloch-operator extraction pipeline is controlled by the single shell slope
\[
v_\parallel.
\]

Its exact projected definition is
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr),
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i.
}
\]

The exact bookkeeping split is
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\]

Here
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}P_*\bigr),
\]
\[
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(
\sigma^3P_*
\left[
(\partial_{p_\parallel}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{p_\parallel}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\right]_{p=0}
P_*
\right),
\]
with \(\mathcal C=\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K\), and
\[
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12\,\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}P_*\bigr),
\]
where \(K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}\) is the derivative of the remote Schur complement.

At the reduced witness level this is equivalent to
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=v_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
c_\parallel=c_\parallel^{(JJ)}+c_\parallel^{(JK)}+c_\parallel^{(KK)}.
}
\]

Thus the longitudinal column is formally closed.
What remains is the explicit insertion of the branch-specific harmonic data entering the three pieces
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Principal Class-II Reduction of the Longitudinal Column}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the Bloch-operator pipeline, the Class-II longitudinal contribution
\[
v_\parallel^{(II)}
\]
still looks broad if one keeps the full \((JJ,JK,KK)\) split.
However, in the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the principal shell-order source classification is already sharp:

\[
JJ \leadsto \text{longitudinal only},
\qquad
JK,KK \leadsto \text{transverse family only}.
\]

Therefore the longitudinal Class-II column reduces to a single piece:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}=v_\parallel^{(II,JJ)}.
}
\]

\section{1. Channel decomposition of the Class-II longitudinal piece}

Starting from the Class-II derivative block
\[
K_\parallel^{(II)},
\]
the shell witness decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
v_\parallel^{(II,JJ)}
+
v_\parallel^{(II,JK)}
+
v_\parallel^{(II,KK)}.
}
\label{eq:vII_channel_split}
\end{equation}

At the reduced witness level, the same decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(II)}
=
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}
+
c_\parallel^{(JK)}
+
c_\parallel^{(KK)},
\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(II)}\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:cpar_channel_split}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Principal shell-order source classification}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the principal shell-order classification is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0,
}
\label{eq:cpar_JK_KK_zero}
\end{equation}
while the pure \(JJ\)-sector is the unique principal Class-II longitudinal source:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}\ \text{is allowed and is the unique principal longitudinal source.}
}
\label{eq:cpar_JJ_unique}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
v_\parallel^{(II,JJ)},
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(II)}=c_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:vII_equals_JJ}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Universal shell-normal form of the pure \(JJ\) block}

The shell-reduced pure-\(JJ\) derivative block has universal shell-normal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(II,J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
}
\label{eq:KJJ_shell_normal}
\end{equation}
where \(M\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix on the tangent doublet space:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\sigma_1
+
m_2\sigma_2
+
m_3\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:M_pauli_decomp}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
K_\parallel^{(II,J)}
=
\hat n^iK_i^{(II,J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,M.
\label{eq:Kpar_JJ}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact longitudinal extraction of the \(JJ\) piece}

By the exact projected longitudinal formula,
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{(II,JJ)}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\sigma_3P_*K_\parallel^{(II,J)}P_*\bigr).
\label{eq:vJJ_trace_start}
\end{equation}

Since \(K_\parallel^{(II,J)}=-\Gamma_J M\), one gets
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{(II,JJ)}
=
-\frac{\Gamma_J}{2}\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M).
\label{eq:vJJ_trace_mid}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3)=0,\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3\sigma_1)=0,\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3\sigma_2)=0,\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3\sigma_3)=2,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II,JJ)}=-\Gamma_J\,m_3.
}
\label{eq:vJJ_final_m3}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal Class-II longitudinal slope is controlled by a single scalar:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_J\,m_3.
}
\label{eq:vII_final_m3}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Equivalent overlap-layer dictionary}

The same longitudinal contribution is also written, in the current explicit branch dictionary, as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,I_{\theta'^3}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2.
}
\label{eq:vII_dictionary_j2}
\end{equation}

Since in the Bloch pipeline one identifies
\[
\lambda_\parallel=v_\parallel,
\]
the principal Class-II longitudinal piece can be equivalently parameterized as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12\,I_{\theta'^3}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2
\qquad
\text{(same \(JJ\)-sector, alternative normalization language).}
}
\label{eq:vII_j2_equiv}
\end{equation}

So the two exact languages for the same principal longitudinal Class-II column are:
\[
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_Jm_3
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12\,I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2.
\]

\section{6. Longitudinal column after the \(JJ\)-reduction}

The full longitudinal column now becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
-\Gamma_J m_3
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_column_reduced}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the overlap-language normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\frac12\,I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_column_j2}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest remaining task}

So the longitudinal column is now reduced to three finite ingredients:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},
\qquad
m_3\ \text{(equiv. }j^2\text{)},
\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_remaining_three}
\end{equation}

What remains open is no longer the channel classification.
It is only the explicit evaluation of these three quantities for the chosen refined locked microscopic branch.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Concrete Formulas for the Bare and Spectator Pieces of the Longitudinal Column}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The longitudinal column has already been reduced to
\[
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

The Class-II piece is already isolated.
So the next nonredundant step is to write the remaining two pieces explicitly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the bare periodic/refined contribution \(v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}\),
\item the remote-Schur spectator contribution \(v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}\).
\end{enumerate}

The important structural point is that the translation-invariant isotropic bare Brazovskii derivative vanishes exactly on the shell.
Therefore the genuinely nontrivial bare longitudinal source must come from the refined periodic/internal \(k\)-dependent part.

\section{1. Canonical decomposition of the triplet Bloch block}

Write the triplet Bloch block as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
+
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}
+
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k).
}
\label{eq:vbare_Hpsipsi_decomp}
\end{equation}
Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}},
}
\label{eq:vbare_Ksplit}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\label{eq:vbare_Kbare_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\label{eq:vbare_Kper0_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:vbare_Kperint_def}
\end{equation}

Since \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}\) is \(k\)-independent,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}=0.
}
\label{eq:vbare_Kper0_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full bare-side derivative contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}.
}
\label{eq:vbare_Kpsipsi_reduced}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Vanishing of the isotropic on-shell derivative}

For the isotropic Brazovskii bare kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_0(q)=r_0+Z|q|^2+Y|q|^4,
}
\label{eq:vbare_h0}
\end{equation}
its derivative is
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)
=
2\bigl(Z+2Y|q|^2\bigr)q_i.
\label{eq:vbare_dh0}
\end{equation}
At the Brazovskii shell
\[
|q|=q_*,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y},
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0.
}
\label{eq:vbare_on_shell_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus the isotropic translation-invariant bare symbol does not generate the first-order shell transport on-shell.
Hence the genuinely nontrivial bare longitudinal source must come from the refined periodic/internal \(k\)-dependent piece
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k).
\]

\section{3. Exact bare longitudinal formula}

The bare longitudinal derivative block is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\hat n_i K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\hat n_i
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:vbare_Kpar_exact}
\end{equation}
where the isotropic on-shell derivative has already dropped out.

Projecting to the low shell slot gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3 P_* K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}} P_*
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:vbare_trace_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the valley-diagonal internal block language,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:vbare_Epm_final}
\end{equation}
where \(E_\pm^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)\) are the two valley-diagonal \(2\times2\) blocks coming from the refined periodic/internal \(\Psi\Psi\)-sector.

\section{4. Exact spectator longitudinal formula}

Let
\[
A(p):=H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(p),
\qquad
R(p):=H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(p)^{-1},
\qquad
B(p):=H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(p).
\]
The remote Schur correction is
\[
-A(p)R(p)B(p).
\]
Differentiating at \(p=0\) in the longitudinal direction gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
-
\left.\partial_{p_\parallel}A(p)\right|_{p=0}R_*B_*
-
A_*R_*\left.\partial_{p_\parallel}B(p)\right|_{p=0}
+
A_*R_*\left.\partial_{p_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(p)\right|_{p=0}R_*B_*,
}
\label{eq:vsp_Kpar_exact}
\end{equation}
where
\[
A_*=A(0),\qquad
B_*=B(0),\qquad
R_*=H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(0)^{-1}.
\]

Projecting this to the low shell slot gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3 P_* K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})} P_*
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:vsp_trace_final}
\end{equation}

This is the exact spectator contribution to the longitudinal shell slope.

\section{5. Final longitudinal column after the concrete reduction}

Combining the already-isolated Class-II piece with the formulas above, the longitudinal column becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})},
}
\label{eq:vpar_final_column_again}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3 P_* K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}} P_*
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:vpar_final_bare_box}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
-\Gamma_J m_3
\qquad
\text{(equivalently, }
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2
\text{ at principal \(JJ\) shell order),}
}
\label{eq:vpar_final_II_box}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3 P_* K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})} P_*
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:vpar_final_sp_box}
\end{equation}

So the remaining longitudinal microscopic frontier has now been reduced to three finite scalar evaluations:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}},
\qquad
m_3\ \text{(or equivalently }j^2\text{)},
\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_three_scalars}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Concrete Reduction of the Longitudinal Column}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The bare longitudinal piece can now be reduced one step further.

The projected periodic/internal shell block satisfies
\[
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
P_*H_0P_*
+
p_i\,\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a
+
O(|p|^2),
\]
so that
\[
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}=\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a.
\]

Hence the bare longitudinal slope is not an abstract derivative anymore.
It is exactly the shell-normal \(\sigma_3\) coefficient
\[
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
\]

\section{1. Bare longitudinal piece as the shell-normal \texorpdfstring{$\sigma_3$}{sigma3} coefficient}

From the projected periodic/internal expansion,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
P_*H_0P_*
+
p_i\,\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a
+
O(|p|^2),
}
\label{eq:long_bare_projected_exp}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}=\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:long_Ki_from_Ntilde}
\end{equation}

Using the exact extraction formula
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}P_*\bigr),
\]
and the fact that the isotropic on-shell derivative has already dropped out, one obtains
\begin{align}
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
&=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3\,\hat n^i \widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&=
\hat n^i\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,3}.
\label{eq:vbare_Ntilde}
\end{align}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}=\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:vbare_final_N3}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Minimal shell tensor basis}

The shell tensor basis is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}
=
\lambda_\parallel\,\hat n_i\delta^{a3}
+
\alpha\,(e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2})
+
\beta\,(-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}).
}
\label{eq:long_min_shell_tensor_basis}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
=
\hat n^i\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,3},
}
\label{eq:Nparallel3_def}
\end{equation}
is exactly the shell-normal longitudinal coefficient in the bare periodic/internal block.

\section{3. Class-II and spectator pieces}

The principal Class-II longitudinal piece is already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_J m_3,
}
\label{eq:long_vII_final_again}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2
}
\label{eq:long_vII_j2_again}
\end{equation}
in the pure-\(JJ\) language.

The spectator piece remains the derivative of the remote Schur complement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3 P_* K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})} P_*
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:long_vsp_again}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final concrete longitudinal column}

Combining everything, the longitudinal column is now
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
-\Gamma_J m_3
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:long_final_concrete_column}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the overlap-language normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})},
}
\label{eq:long_final_concrete_column_overlap}
\end{equation}
up to the sign convention absorbed into the definition of the pure-\(JJ\) coefficient.

\section{5. Honest remaining microscopic inputs}

So the longitudinal column has been reduced to exactly three finite scalar inputs:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3},
\qquad
m_3\ \text{(equiv.\ }j^2\text{)},
\qquad
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:long_three_remaining_scalars}
\end{equation}

No additional channel classification remains.
The next microscopic task is only the explicit evaluation of these three quantities in the chosen refined locked branch.

\section{Concrete Bare and Spectator Longitudinal Formulas in the Bloch-Operator Pipeline}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The longitudinal column is now reduced to three finite pieces:
\[
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

The Class-II piece has already been isolated to the principal \(JJ\)-sector.
So the remaining task is to make the bare and spectator pieces completely explicit.

The key point is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the only live bare first-order triplet source is the \(k\)-dependent periodic/internal block \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\);
\item the spectator piece is exactly the derivative of the Schur-renormalized pair-diagonal blocks \(E_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Bare longitudinal source: only \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\) survives}

The triplet-sector audit gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
=
\underbrace{H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)}_{\text{dead in }K_i}
+
\underbrace{H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}}_{\text{dead in }K_i}
+
\underbrace{H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)}_{\text{only live triplet source}}.
}
\label{eq:long_triplet_audit_table}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact live triplet-sector derivative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:long_Kbare_live}
\end{equation}

The corresponding bare longitudinal shell slope is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(
\sigma^3 P_*K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}P_*
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:long_vbare_live}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the pair-diagonal valley notation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:long_vbare_pairdiag}
\end{equation}
where \(E_\pm^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)\) are the \(2\times2\) pair-diagonal blocks induced by \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\).

Thus the bare longitudinal column is completely localized to the shell-compatible \(k\)-linear harmonic matrix elements of \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\) at \(k=k_*\).

\section{2. Spectator elimination: exact pair-diagonal formulas}

The finite shell matrix has the exact block form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p) & C_+(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p) & C_-(p)\\
C_+(p)^\dagger & C_-(p)^\dagger & H_{ss}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:long_Hshell_exact}
\end{equation}

After exact spectator elimination, the core effective Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
-
\begin{pmatrix}
C_+(p)\\
C_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)
\begin{pmatrix}
C_+(p)^\dagger & C_-(p)^\dagger
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:long_coreeff_exact}
\end{equation}
with
\[
R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)=\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}.
\]

Therefore the renormalized pair-diagonal blocks are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_+(p)-C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger,
}
\label{eq:long_Eplus_eff}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_-(p)-C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:long_Eminus_eff}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact spectator longitudinal slope}

By definition, the spectator contribution to the longitudinal shell slope is the part of the pair-diagonal slope coming from the Schur correction in \eqref{eq:long_Eplus_eff}--\eqref{eq:long_Eminus_eff}.

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
-\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
-
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:long_vsp_pairdiag}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, writing
\[
A(p):=\binom{C_+(p)}{C_-(p)},
\qquad
R(p):=R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p),
\]
this is the same spectator derivative already obtained from the general Schur-complement formula.

\section{4. Full longitudinal column in fully concrete form}

Combining the bare, Class-II, and spectator pieces, we obtain the fully concrete longitudinal column:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}
\;+\;
v_\parallel^{(II)}
\;-\;
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
-
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:long_vpar_fully_concrete}
\end{equation}

At principal shell order, the Class-II piece is already reduced to the pure-\(JJ\) sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_J m_3,
}
\label{eq:long_vII_gammaJm3_again}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2.
}
\label{eq:long_vII_j2_again2}
\end{equation}

Therefore the remaining microscopic longitudinal inputs are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p),
\qquad
m_3\ \text{(equiv.\ }j^2\text{)},
\qquad
C_\pm(p),\ R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p).
}
\label{eq:long_final_inputs}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Honest endpoint of the current pipeline stage}

No further structural reorganization is needed.

The longitudinal column has now been reduced to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a bare pair-diagonal shell slope from \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\),
\item a pure-\(JJ\) Class-II shell slope,
\item a spectator-renormalized pair-diagonal shell slope from the exact Schur correction.
\end{enumerate}

So the next legitimate step inside the Bloch-operator pipeline is the actual insertion of these explicit block matrix elements, not another abstract reduction.

\section{Final summary}

The longitudinal column in the Bloch-operator extraction pipeline is now fully concrete:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\]

The bare piece is localized entirely to the shell-compatible \(k\)-linear periodic/internal block:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0},
}
\]
equivalently
\[
K_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

The principal Class-II piece is already reduced to the pure-\(JJ\) sector:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_Jm_3,
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2.
}
\]

The spectator piece is the exact pair-diagonal Schur-renormalized slope:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
-\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
-
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\]

Therefore the remaining longitudinal microscopic inputs are exactly
\[
\boxed{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p),
\qquad
m_3\ \text{(equiv.\ }j^2\text{)},
\qquad
C_\pm(p),\ R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p).
}
\]

No further structural reduction is needed.
The next step is the explicit insertion of these block matrix elements.

\section{Bare Longitudinal Source is Not Symmetry-Forced to Vanish}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The next decisive question is whether the bare longitudinal slope
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
\]
is forced to vanish by symmetry.

The answer is no.

The bare longitudinal piece is defined through the pair-diagonal shell difference
\[
D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)=\frac12\bigl(E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)\bigr),
\]
hence
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
\right|_{p=0}.
\]

If the opposite valley is related by \(p\mapsto -p\), then
\[
E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)=E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(-p),
\]
so
\[
D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
=
\frac12\bigl(E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(-p)\bigr).
\]
Therefore
\[
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
\right|_{p=0}
=
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\]
which is not symmetry-forced to vanish.

Thus \(v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}=0\) would require an additional tuning, not merely the valley symmetry itself.

\section{1. Exact pair-diagonal definition}

The bare longitudinal shell slope is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:bare_pairdiag_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Valley relation does not force cancellation}

Assume the opposite-valley bare blocks satisfy
\begin{equation}
E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)=E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(-p).
\label{eq:bare_valley_relation}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{align}
D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
&=
\frac12\bigl(E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12\bigl(E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(-p)\bigr).
\label{eq:bare_D_as_odd}
\end{align}

Differentiating at \(p=0\),
\begin{equation}
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
\right|_{p=0}
=
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\label{eq:bare_no_cancellation}
\end{equation}
so the valley relation doubles the odd slope rather than cancelling it.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}=0
\quad\text{is not symmetry-forced.}
}
\label{eq:bare_not_forbidden}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Shell-tensor form}

After shell projection, the refined periodic/internal block satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
P_*H_0P_*
+
p_i\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a
+
O(|p|^2),
}
\label{eq:bare_shell_tensor_exp}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}=\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:bare_shell_tensor_K}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:bare_v_as_N3}
\end{equation}

So the vanishing of the bare longitudinal piece is equivalent to
\[
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}=0,
\]
which is an actual microscopic coefficient statement, not a symmetry theorem.

\section{4. Consequence for the full longitudinal column}

The full longitudinal column now reads
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
-\Gamma_J m_3
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:full_long_column_after_bare}
\end{equation}

Hence the remaining nontrivial microscopic question is not whether the bare piece is symmetry-forbidden.
It is whether the spectator piece survives or vanishes in the chosen working truncation.

\section{Final summary}

The bare longitudinal shell slope is
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\]

If the opposite-valley relation is
\[
E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)=E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(-p),
\]
then the pair-diagonal difference is
\[
D^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)=\frac12\bigl(E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(-p)\bigr),
\]
and therefore its longitudinal derivative at \(p=0\) does not cancel.
So
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}=0
\text{ is not symmetry-forced.}
}
\]

After shell projection,
\[
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
P_*H_0P_*+p_i\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^{\,a}\sigma_a+O(|p|^2),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}=\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
}
\]

Therefore the full longitudinal column is now concretely
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
-\Gamma_J m_3
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\]

The next nonredundant microscopic task is to determine whether the spectator contribution
\[
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
\]
vanishes in the present working truncation or provides an additional independent longitudinal source.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Spectator Longitudinal Piece in the One-Step Scalar Spectator Closure}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the current Bloch-operator pipeline, the spectator longitudinal term is
\[
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
-\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
-
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
\]

In the one-step scalar spectator closure already written in the notes, the spectator block is scalar on the internal doublet and the core-to-spectator couplings are equal for the \(+\) and \(-\) core pair.
As a result, the two diagonal Schur renormalizations coincide identically, so their difference has zero longitudinal derivative.

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}=0
}
\]
in the current one-step scalar spectator truncation.

\section{1. Exact spectator formula}

The renormalized pair-diagonal blocks are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_+(p)-C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger,
}
\label{eq:sp_Eplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_-(p)-C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:sp_Eminus}
\end{equation}
Hence the spectator contribution to the longitudinal slope is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
-\frac12
\left.
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\frac{
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
-
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
}{2}
\right]
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:sp_v_formula}
\end{equation}

\section{2. One-step scalar spectator shell}

In the one-step shell closure, the spectator matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{1step}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_c & m & g & g & g & g\\
m & E_c & g & g & g & g\\
g & g & E_s & 0 & 0 & 0\\
g & g & 0 & E_s & 0 & 0\\
g & g & 0 & 0 & E_s & 0\\
g & g & 0 & 0 & 0 & E_s
\end{pmatrix}
\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
O(A^4),
}
\label{eq:sp_H1step}
\end{equation}
with a single symmetric spectator combination
\[
|S\rangle=\frac12\sum_{a=1}^4|\eta_a\rangle
\]
coupled to the core pair, while the other three spectator combinations decouple.

Crucially, the spectator shell is scalar on the internal doublet:
\[
H_{ss}(p)\propto \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)\propto \mathbf 1_2.
\]

Moreover, by cubic symmetry and equal amplitudes, the \(+\) and \(-\) core pair couple to the same symmetric spectator combination with the same scalar amplitude \(g\).
Therefore, at the one-step scalar level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+(p)=C_-(p)=:C_{\mathrm{sp}}(p)
}
\label{eq:sp_Cplus_equals_Cminus}
\end{equation}
up to the common internal spectator factor \(\mathbf 1_2\).

\section{3. Exact cancellation of the diagonal spectator difference}

Substituting \eqref{eq:sp_Cplus_equals_Cminus} into the Schur corrections gives
\begin{equation}
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
=
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:sp_diag_equal}
\end{equation}
Hence the spectator contribution to the pair-diagonal difference vanishes identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
-
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
=0.
}
\label{eq:sp_diff_zero}
\end{equation}

Differentiating \eqref{eq:sp_diff_zero} with respect to \(p_\parallel\) and inserting into \eqref{eq:sp_v_formula}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}=0.
}
\label{eq:sp_v_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Consequence for the longitudinal column}

Therefore, in the present one-step scalar spectator truncation, the longitudinal column collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}.
}
\label{eq:sp_long_column_reduced}
\end{equation}

Using the previously derived formulas,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\qquad
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_J m_3,
}
\label{eq:sp_two_source_form}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
-\Gamma_J m_3.
}
\label{eq:sp_final_long_column}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the overlap-language normalization of the pure-\(JJ\) branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
