=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:sp_final_long_column_overlap}
\end{equation}
up to the fixed sign convention between \(\Gamma_J m_3\) and the \(j^2\)-normalization.

\section{5. Honest status}

What is proved here is exact for the current one-step scalar spectator closure:
\[
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}=0.

What is not yet proved in complete generality is that every possible enlarged spectator completion beyond this truncation preserves the same cancellation.

\qquad

}
\label{eq:sp_remaining_two}
\end{equation}

v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}

In the current one-step scalar spectator closure,

the spectator shell is scalar on the internal doublet, and the \(+\) and \(-\) core states couple to the same symmetric spectator combination with equal scalar amplitude.

\section{3. Generic nondegeneracy theorem}

\section{Actual Finite Extraction Protocol for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel$}{L*=mparallel uparallel}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, the longitudinal Bloch-operator pipeline is no longer a broad operator problem.
It has been reduced to the explicit finite extraction of two scalars:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

These are obtained directly from:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the two projected valley-diagonal \(2\times2\) blocks \(E_\pm(0)\),
\item the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix \(\mathcal U_j(0)\),
\item the background selector \(m_\parallel=m^3(P_0)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Projected valley-diagonal blocks}

Fix the enriched shell carrier basis
\[
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]

The two valley-diagonal projected matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_Epm}
\end{equation}

Let \(\eta_\pm\) be the normalized low eigenvectors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+(0)\eta_+=\varepsilon_+\eta_+,
\qquad
E_-(0)\eta_-=\varepsilon_-\eta_-,
\qquad
\|\eta_\pm\|=1.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_eta}
\end{equation}

Write
\[
\eta_+=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(+)}\\
A_2^{(+)}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\eta_-=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(-)}\\
A_2^{(-)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the valley Bloch asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_Delta00}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix}

Define the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
a,b=1,2.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_Uj}
\end{equation}

Project to the shell-normal direction:
\[
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0).
\]
Then the shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_upar}
\end{equation}

This avoids any raw trace notation and is the safest executable formula.

\section{3. Background selector}

In the canonical locked basis, the background selector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_mpar}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_Lstar}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Insertion into the longitudinal column}

The current working-truncation longitudinal column is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_vpar_insert1}
\end{equation}

In the canonical branch, the pure-\(JJ\) harmonic is controlled by \(L_*\), so the dominant first-shell term is governed by
\[
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
\]
Therefore the practical dominant longitudinal criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}\,
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}
\right|
>
\left|
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}R_N
\right|.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_dom_criterion}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:DeltaL_dom_criterion} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=v_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Ultra-minimal first-shell form}

In the ultra-minimal first-shell truncation \(R_N=0\), the longitudinal column reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_ultramin}
\end{equation}

If one moreover works in the dominant \(JJ\)-calibrated branch where the second term is the load-bearing one, then the sufficient condition simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:DeltaL_ultra_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final executable checklist}

The final finite execution order is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build the two \(2\times2\) valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\);
\item diagonalize them and extract \(\eta_\pm\), hence \(\Delta_{00}\);
\item build the reduced intervalley matrix \(\mathcal U_j(0)\);
\item compute
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr];
\]
\item read \(m_\parallel=m^3(P_0)\);
\item form \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\);
\item insert \(\Delta_{00}\) and \(L_*\) into \eqref{eq:DeltaL_vpar_insert1}.
\end{enumerate}

No further structural reduction is required.
The remaining problem is now a literal finite projected matrix-element computation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Effective worldvolume Weyl equation}

The reduced carrier equation on the defect worldvolume is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left[
i\partial_t
-\lambda_\parallel\,\hat n^\mu \sigma_3 \partial_\mu
-\alpha\,E^{\mu}{}_{a}\sigma_a \partial_\mu
-\beta\,J^{\mu}{}_{a}\sigma_a \partial_\mu
\right]\chi=0,
\qquad a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:effective_weyl_worldvolume}
\end{equation}

\section{Adapted-frame form}

Choosing the adapted orthonormal frame
\[
(\hat n,e_1,e_2),
\]
the equation becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left[
i\partial_t
-\lambda_\parallel \sigma_3 \partial_\parallel
-\alpha(\sigma_1\partial_1+\sigma_2\partial_2)
-\beta(-\sigma_1\partial_2+\sigma_2\partial_1)
\right]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:effective_weyl_adapted}
\end{equation}

\section{Dispersion relation}

For a plane-wave mode
\[
\chi=u\,e^{-i\omega t+i(p_\parallel x_\parallel+p_1x_1+p_2x_2)},
\]
the reduced Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\sigma_2.
\label{eq:Hp_reduced}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega_\pm(p)
=
\pm
\sqrt{
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2)
}.
}
\label{eq:dispersion_reduced}
\end{equation}

\section{Interpretation}

Equation \eqref{eq:effective_weyl_worldvolume} is the effective massless anisotropic chiral Dirac/Weyl equation on the defect worldvolume.

If
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\]
then the dispersion relation is conical:
\[
\omega_\pm(p)
=
\pm
\sqrt{
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2)
}.
\]

If in addition no symmetry-allowed constant mass term survives, then this defines a protected massless chiral carrier localized on the defect.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact General \(2\times2\) Hermitian Formula for \(\Delta_{00}\)}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Let the two valley-diagonal projected blocks be arbitrary Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrices:
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & b_\pm\\
\overline{b_\pm} & d_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
a_\pm,d_\pm\in\mathbb R,\quad b_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

Then the lower eigenvalues and normalized lower eigenvectors can be written in closed form.
Hence the intervalley Bloch asymmetry
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-
\]
is also obtained in closed form.

This turns the longitudinal zero condition into an explicit finite cancellation equation in the microscopic matrix entries of \(E_\pm(0)\).

\section{1. General Hermitian valley blocks}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & b_\pm\\
\overline{b_\pm} & d_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
a_\pm,d_\pm\in\mathbb R,\quad b_\pm\in\mathbb C.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_Epm}
\end{equation}

Define the spectral gaps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\pm^{\mathrm{spec}}
:=
\sqrt{(a_\pm-d_\pm)^2+4|b_\pm|^2}.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_gap}
\end{equation}

The lower eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\pm
=
\frac{a_\pm+d_\pm-\Delta_\pm^{\mathrm{spec}}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_loweval}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Canonically normalized lower eigenvectors}

Assume first that \(b_\pm\neq0\).
Then a canonical lower-eigenvector representative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{N_\pm}
\begin{pmatrix}
b_\pm\\
X_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
X_\pm:=\varepsilon_\pm-a_\pm,
\qquad
N_\pm:=\sqrt{|b_\pm|^2+X_\pm^2}.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_eta}
\end{equation}

Indeed,
\[
E_\pm(0)
\begin{pmatrix}
b_\pm\\
X_\pm
\end{pmatrix}
=
\varepsilon_\pm
\begin{pmatrix}
b_\pm\\
X_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Since \(\varepsilon_\pm,a_\pm\in\mathbb R\), the numbers \(X_\pm\) are real:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_\pm
=
\frac{d_\pm-a_\pm-\Delta_\pm^{\mathrm{spec}}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_Xpm}
\end{equation}

Thus the normalized lower eigenvectors are completely explicit in the matrix entries.

\section{3. Exact closed formula for \(\Delta_{00}\)}

Recall
\[
\Sigma_3=
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:gen2x2_eta},
\begin{align}
\Delta_{00}
&=
\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac{1}{N_+N_-}
\begin{pmatrix}
\overline{b_+} & X_+
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
b_-\\
X_-
\end{pmatrix}
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}{N_+N_-}.
\label{eq:gen2x2_Delta00_raw}
\end{align}

Therefore the exact general closed formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}},
\qquad
X_\pm=\frac{d_\pm-a_\pm-\Delta_\pm^{\mathrm{spec}}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_Delta00_final}
\end{equation}

This is the desired fully general \(2\times2\) Hermitian formula.

\section{4. Exact zero condition for \(\Delta_{00}\)}

From \eqref{eq:gen2x2_Delta00_final}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{b_+}b_-=X_+X_-.
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence vanishing of \(\Delta_{00}\) is not automatic.
It is an explicit algebraic cancellation condition between the two valley-block entries.

In particular, within the space of all matrix entries \((a_\pm,d_\pm,b_\pm)\), the condition
\[
\overline{b_+}b_-=X_+X_-
\]
is an exact finite tuning relation.

\section{5. Degenerate/off-diagonal special cases}

If \(b_\pm=0\), the matrix is already diagonal:
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm&0\\
0&d_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then:

\begin{itemize}
\item if \(a_\pm<d_\pm\), the lower eigenvector is \((1,0)^T\),
\item if \(d_\pm<a_\pm\), the lower eigenvector is \((0,1)^T\),
\item if \(a_\pm=d_\pm\), the lower eigenspace is degenerate and \(\eta_\pm\) is not uniquely fixed until an additional convention is imposed.
\end{itemize}

Thus the formula \eqref{eq:gen2x2_Delta00_final} is the nondegenerate generic case, while the diagonal/degenerate case must be handled separately by the obvious basis choice.

\section{6. Insertion into the longitudinal column}

The current working-truncation longitudinal column is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_vpar_start}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:gen2x2_Delta00_final}, we obtain the fully explicit finite formula
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\right].
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_vpar_explicit}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact longitudinal zero condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\right].
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_vpar_zero}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal failure condition is now an explicit finite cancellation equation in the microscopic entries of the two Hermitian valley blocks, together with the \(JJ\)-harmonic and remainder data.

\section{7. Dominant canonical branch form}

In the canonical first-shell dominant branch,
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]
Therefore the dominant longitudinal column becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{dom}}
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
}
\label{eq:gen2x2_vpar_dom}
\end{equation}
up to the explicit harmonic remainder \(R_N\).

Thus the longitudinal problem is fully reduced to a finite matrix-and-scalar insertion problem.

\section{Final summary}

For completely general Hermitian valley blocks
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & b_\pm\\
\overline{b_\pm} & d_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
a_\pm,d_\pm\in\mathbb R,\quad b_\pm\in\mathbb C,
\]
the lower eigenvalues are
\[
\varepsilon_\pm
=
\frac{a_\pm+d_\pm-\sqrt{(a_\pm-d_\pm)^2+4|b_\pm|^2}}{2},
\]
and a canonical normalized lower eigenvector is
\[
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{|b_\pm|^2+X_\pm^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
b_\pm\\
X_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
X_\pm=\varepsilon_\pm-a_\pm.
\]

Hence the intervalley Bloch asymmetry has the exact closed form
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{b_+}b_-=X_+X_-,
\]
so vanishing of \(\Delta_{00}\) is an explicit finite algebraic cancellation condition.

Substituting this into the longitudinal column gives
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\right].
}
\]

Thus the longitudinal failure condition is now a fully explicit finite cancellation equation in the microscopic entries of the two \(2\times2\) Hermitian valley blocks, together with the \(JJ\)-harmonic and remainder data.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact General \(2\times2\) Matrix Formula for \texorpdfstring{$L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel$}{L*=mparallel uparallel}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal scalar
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
\]
is extracted from the shell-normal reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix.

The key point is that one does not need any further structural assumptions to write \(u_\parallel\) in closed form.
If
\[
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
\]
is treated as a completely general \(2\times2\) complex matrix, then \(u_\parallel\) is simply its \(\Sigma_3\)-coefficient, i.e. its diagonal asymmetry.

This gives an exact fully finite formula for \(L_*\).

\section{1. General shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix}

Define the shell-normal projected reduced intervalley matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_Uparallel_def}
\end{equation}

Write it as a completely general \(2\times2\) complex matrix:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_{ab}\in\mathbb C.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_general_Up}
\end{equation}

No further reduction is needed to write the shell-normal singlet coefficient.

\section{2. Pauli decomposition of a general \(2\times2\) matrix}

Any \(2\times2\) complex matrix has the unique decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_\parallel
=
c_0\,\mathbf 1_2
+
c_1\,\Sigma_1
+
c_2\,\Sigma_2
+
c_3\,\Sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Lstar_Pauli_decomp}
\end{equation}
with coefficients
\begin{align}
\boxed{
c_0=\frac{u_{11}+u_{22}}{2},
}
\label{eq:Lstar_c0}
\\
\boxed{
c_1=\frac{u_{12}+u_{21}}{2},
}
\label{eq:Lstar_c1}
\\
\boxed{
c_2=\frac{u_{21}-u_{12}}{2i},
}
\label{eq:Lstar_c2}
\\
\boxed{
c_3=\frac{u_{11}-u_{22}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_c3}
\end{align}

The shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias is precisely the \(\Sigma_3\)-coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel=c_3=\frac{u_{11}-u_{22}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_uparallel_general}
\end{equation}

Thus \(u_\parallel\) is exactly the diagonal asymmetry of the shell-normal reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix.

\section{3. Hermitian special case}

If \(\mathcal U_\parallel\) is Hermitian, then
\[
u_{22}\in\mathbb R,\qquad
u_{11}\in\mathbb R,\qquad
u_{21}=\overline{u_{12}},
\]
and the Pauli coefficients satisfy
\[
c_0,c_1,c_2,c_3\in\mathbb R.
\]

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel=\frac{u_{11}-u_{22}}{2}\in\mathbb R.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_uparallel_herm}
\end{equation}

So the Hermitian case is just the real specialization of the general formula \eqref{eq:Lstar_uparallel_general}.

\section{4. Final exact formula for \(L_*\)}

The background selector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_mparallel_again}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_general_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Lstar_diagdiff_again}
\end{equation}

This is the exact general \(2\times2\) matrix formula for \(L_*\).

\section{5. Exact zero condition for \(L_*\)}

From \eqref{eq:Lstar_general_final},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_zero_condition}
\end{equation}

Hence vanishing of \(L_*\) is not automatic.
It is an explicit finite algebraic condition on the shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix and the background selector.

\section{6. Full finite longitudinal audit with both scalars inserted}

The current working-truncation longitudinal column is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_vpar_start}
\end{equation}

From the general Hermitian formula for the valley asymmetry,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}},
}
\label{eq:Lstar_Delta_insert}
\end{equation}
where
\[
X_\pm
=
\frac{d_\pm-a_\pm-\sqrt{(a_\pm-d_\pm)^2+4|b_\pm|^2}}{2},
\]
and from \eqref{eq:Lstar_general_final},
\[
L_*=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}),
\]
the dominant canonical branch term
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}
\]
becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_VJJ_insert}
\end{equation}

Therefore the fully explicit finite longitudinal column can be written schematically as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\alpha_X\,\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,A_{G_*}
+
R_N
\right],
}
\label{eq:Lstar_vpar_fully_finite}
\end{equation}
up to the fixed branch-normalization factor relating \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\) to \(\alpha_XL_*A_{G_*}\).

\section{7. Final finite cancellation equation}

Hence the exact longitudinal failure condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\alpha_X\,\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,A_{G_*}
+
R_N
\right].
}
\label{eq:Lstar_full_zero}
\end{equation}

This is a completely finite cancellation equation in the microscopic matrix entries of
\[
E_\pm(0),
\qquad
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\]
together with
\[
m_\parallel,\qquad
A_{G_*},\qquad
R_N,\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
\]

\section{8. Honest status}

At this point, both remaining carrier-side longitudinal scalars are closed in general finite matrix form:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}},
\qquad
L_*=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_both_scalars_final}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal frontier is no longer structural at all.
It is a literal finite insertion problem for the matrix entries of
\[
E_\pm(0),\qquad \hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\]
and the remaining scalar data
\[
m_\parallel,\qquad A_{G_*},\qquad R_N,\qquad \widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
\]

\section{Final summary}

For a completely general shell-normal reduced intervalley matrix
\[
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
the shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias is exactly the \(\Sigma_3\)-coefficient:
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel=\frac{u_{11}-u_{22}}{2}.
}
\]

Therefore the longitudinal scalar is
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Hence
\[
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22},
\]
so vanishing of \(L_*\) is an explicit finite algebraic condition.

Together with the exact general Hermitian formula
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}},
}
\]
the longitudinal column becomes a fully explicit finite insertion problem.

Thus both remaining carrier-side longitudinal scalars are now closed in completely general finite matrix form:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

\section{Actual Finite Insertion of the Two Remaining Longitudinal Scalars}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The longitudinal frontier is no longer structural.
It is now a literal finite insertion problem for the projected shell matrix elements.

The next executable step is to compute:
\[
E_+(0),\qquad
E_-(0),\qquad
\mathcal U_j(0),\qquad
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
\]
and then form
\[
\Delta_{00},\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

\section{1. Explicit shell carrier basis}

Fix the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
and the enriched shell carrier basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:ins_basis}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the shell harmonic basis \(|G,r\rangle\),
\[
|+,a\rangle=\sum_r \chi_{a,r}|G_*,r\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle=\sum_r \chi_{a,r}|-G_*,r\rangle.
\]

\section{2. Actual valley-diagonal \(2\times2\) blocks}

The two projected valley-diagonal blocks are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:ins_Epm_def}
\end{equation}

In shell-harmonic components this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\sum_{r,r'}
\overline{\chi_{a,r}}\,
\mathcal H_{(G_*,r),(G_*,r')}(k_*)\,
\chi_{b,r'},
}
\label{eq:ins_Eplus_components}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\sum_{r,r'}
\overline{\chi_{a,r}}\,
\mathcal H_{(-G_*,r),(-G_*,r')}(k_*)\,
\chi_{b,r'}.
}
\label{eq:ins_Eminus_components}
\end{equation}

Write them as general Hermitian matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & b_\pm\\
\overline{b_\pm} & d_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
a_\pm,d_\pm\in\mathbb R,\quad
b_\pm\in\mathbb C.
}
\label{eq:ins_Epm_general}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact extraction of \(\Delta_{00}\)}

Let \(\eta_\pm\) be the normalized lower eigenvectors:
\[
E_\pm(0)\eta_\pm=\varepsilon_\pm\eta_\pm.
\]

Define
\[
\Delta_\pm^{\mathrm{spec}}
=
\sqrt{(a_\pm-d_\pm)^2+4|b_\pm|^2},
\qquad
X_\pm
=
\frac{d_\pm-a_\pm-\Delta_\pm^{\mathrm{spec}}}{2}.
\]
Then a canonical normalized lower eigenvector is
\[
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{|b_\pm|^2+X_\pm^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
b_\pm\\
X_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Hence the exact intervalley Bloch asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}.
}
\label{eq:ins_Delta00_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{b_+}b_-=X_+X_-.
}
\label{eq:ins_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Actual reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix}

Define the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:ins_Uj_def}
\end{equation}

In shell-harmonic components,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\sum_{r,r'}
\overline{\chi_{a,r}}\,
\bigl[\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)\bigr]_{rr'}\,
\chi_{b,r'}.
}
\label{eq:ins_Uj_components}
\end{equation}

Project to the shell-normal direction:
\[
\mathcal U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0).
\]

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:ins_Uparallel_general}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac{u_{11}-u_{22}}{2}
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:ins_uparallel_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Actual extraction of \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\)}

The background selector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:ins_mparallel}
\end{equation}

Therefore the second longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:ins_Lstar_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\label{eq:ins_Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Direct insertion into the longitudinal column}

At the current working-truncation level, the longitudinal column is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ins_vpar_start}
\end{equation}

In the canonical branch,
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
\]
Therefore the dominant first-shell term becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\alpha_X\,
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,
A_{G_*},
}
\label{eq:ins_dom_product}
\end{equation}
up to the fixed branch-normalization factor and the explicit remainder \(R_N\).

Thus the longitudinal zero condition is the finite cancellation equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:ins_final_zero}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}},
\qquad
L_*=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
\]

\section{7. Final executable order}

The actual finite execution order is now completely fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the shell matrix elements \eqref{eq:ins_Eplus_components} and \eqref{eq:ins_Eminus_components};
\item read off \(a_\pm,d_\pm,b_\pm\), then compute \(\Delta_{00}\) from \eqref{eq:ins_Delta00_exact};
\item compute the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix elements \eqref{eq:ins_Uj_components};
\item read off \(u_{11},u_{22}\), then compute \(L_*\) from \eqref{eq:ins_Lstar_exact};
\item read \(m_\parallel=m^3(P_0)\);
\item insert \(\Delta_{00}\) and \(L_*\) into \eqref{eq:ins_vpar_start}.
\end{enumerate}

No further structural theorem is needed.
The remaining task is a literal projected matrix-element computation.

\section{Actual Constant-Envelope Insertion Form of the Final Longitudinal Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

In the constant-envelope branch, the zero-harmonic vectors are already the carrier coefficients in the internal basis \(\{\xi_1,\xi_2\}\).
So the remaining longitudinal scalars are no longer abstract:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Delta_{00}\) is the \(\Sigma_3\)-weighted overlap of the two valley coefficient vectors;
\item \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\) is the shell-normal diagonal asymmetry of the reduced \(J\)-block multiplied by the background selector.
\end{enumerate}

This gives the most concrete final insertion formula presently available inside the Bloch-operator pipeline.

\section{1. Constant-envelope carrier vectors}

Choose the internal basis \(\{\xi_1,\xi_2\}\) and write the selected low carrier coefficients as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_+=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(+)}\\
A_2^{(+)}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\eta_-=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(-)}\\
A_2^{(-)}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:ce_eta_pm_final}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:ce_Delta00_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if the valley-diagonal projected blocks are written as
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & b_\pm\\
\overline{b_\pm} & d_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}},
}
\label{eq:ce_Delta00_2x2}
\end{equation}
with
\[
X_\pm
=
\frac{d_\pm-a_\pm-\sqrt{(a_\pm-d_\pm)^2+4|b_\pm|^2}}{2}.
\]

\section{2. Reduced intervalley \(J\)-block}

Define the reduced \(J\)-matrix on the carrier:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\bigl(\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)\bigr)_{a,b=1}^2,
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:ce_Uj_final}
\end{equation}

Project to the shell-normal direction:
\[
\mathcal U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0).
\]
Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:ce_Uparallel_final}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-normal singlet bias is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac{u_{11}-u_{22}}{2}
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:ce_uparallel_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Final scalar \(L_*\)}

The background selector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:ce_mparallel_final}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:ce_Lstar_final}
\end{equation}

So
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\label{eq:ce_Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final longitudinal column in finite insertion form}

The current working-truncation longitudinal column is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ce_vparallel_start}
\end{equation}

In the canonical branch,
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
\]
Therefore the dominant first-shell term becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}
=
\left(
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}
\right)
\alpha_X\,
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,
A_{G_*},
}
\label{eq:ce_dom_product_vector}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}
=
\frac{\overline{b_+}b_- - X_+X_-}
{\sqrt{|b_+|^2+X_+^2}\,\sqrt{|b_-|^2+X_-^2}}
\,
\alpha_X\,
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,
A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:ce_dom_product_matrix}
\end{equation}

Thus the fully finite longitudinal column is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
+
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,A_{G_*}
+
R_N
\right],
}
\label{eq:ce_vparallel_finite}
\end{equation}
up to the fixed branch-normalization factor relating \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\) to \(\alpha_XL_*A_{G_*}\).

\section{5. Final finite cancellation equation}

Hence the longitudinal failure condition is the explicit finite equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\left[
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,A_{G_*}
+
R_N
\right].
}
\label{eq:ce_longitudinal_zero}
\end{equation}

This is no longer a conceptual obstruction.
It is a finite algebraic cancellation relation among
\[
E_\pm(0),\qquad
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),\qquad
m_\parallel,\qquad
A_{G_*},\qquad
R_N,\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^{\,3}.
\]

\section{Literal Component Assembly for the Final Longitudinal Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

No further structural theorem is needed.
The remaining task is the literal component assembly of the two projected valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\) and the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix \(\mathcal U_j(0)\).

This is the last actual microscopic insertion step inside the Bloch-operator extraction pipeline.

\section{1. Fixed enriched shell carrier basis}

Fix the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
and the enriched shell carrier basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:literal_basis}
\end{equation}

Expand the internal carrier vectors in a fixed shell internal basis \(\{\xi_r\}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_a=\sum_r \chi_{a,r}\,\xi_r.
}
\label{eq:literal_chi_expand}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
|+,a\rangle=\sum_r \chi_{a,r}\,|G_*,\xi_r\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle=\sum_r \chi_{a,r}\,|-G_*,\xi_r\rangle.
\]

\section{2. Literal component formula for the two valley blocks}

The two projected valley-diagonal blocks are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:literal_Epm_def}
\end{equation}

In shell-harmonic components:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=

\overline{\chi_{a,r}}\,
\bigl[H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\bigr]_{(G_*,r),(G_*,r')}
\,\chi_{b,r'},

\label{eq:literal_Eplus_comp}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=

\bigl[H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\bigr]_{(-G_*,r),(-G_*,r')}
\,\chi_{b,r'}.
}
\label{eq:literal_Eminus_comp}
\end{equation}

Thus the only microscopic input needed for \(E_\pm(0)\) is the shell-block matrix of \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\) at the two valley harmonics \(\pm G_*\).

\section{3. Literal component formula for the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix}

\begin{equation}

(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}

(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}

\bigl[\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)\bigr]_{rr'}
\,\chi_{b,r'}.

Projecting to the shell-normal direction gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\bigl(\mathcal U_{\parallel,ab}\bigr)_{a,b=1}^2.

\label{eq:literal_Uparallel}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final finite formulas for the two longitudinal scalars}

\subsection*{(a) Valley Bloch asymmetry}

\[
E_\pm(0)\eta_\pm=\varepsilon_\pm\eta_\pm,

u_\parallel
=

-

\section{5. Final insertion into the longitudinal witness}

The practical first-shell dominant sufficient condition is

\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:literal_suff}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:literal_ultramin}
\end{equation}

So the literal computation target is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl[H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\bigr]_{(\pm G_*,r),(\pm G_*,r')},
\qquad

\qquad
m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:literal_target}
\end{equation}

\section{Comparison of \texorpdfstring{$\rho_{\mathrm{II}}$}{rhoII} and \texorpdfstring{$\rho_{12}$}{rho12} in the Natural TECT Parameter Region}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The explicit one-mediator Class II branch gives
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{II}}
=
\frac{|v_\parallel|}{|v_\perp|}
=
\frac{g_X^2A^3|G_*|^2}{8|Z|M_X^2},
\]
whereas the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC shell-sum branch gives
\[
\rho_{12}
=
\frac{|v_\parallel^{(12)}|}{|v_\perp^{(12)}|}
=
\frac{|g|A^3}{|Z|q_*^2}.
\]

Thus
\[
\frac{\rho_{\mathrm{II}}}{\rho_{12}}
=
\frac{g_X^2|G_*|^2q_*^2}{8|g|M_X^2}
\sim
\frac{g_X^2q_*^4}{8|g|M_X^2}.
\]

Since the Class II mediator is naturally interpreted as heavy in the TECT working branch, the factor \(1/M_X^2\) generically suppresses \(\rho_{\mathrm{II}}\).
Therefore, unless one enters a strong-coupling / not-so-heavy regime,
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{12}>\rho_{\mathrm{II}}
}
\]
is the natural generic ordering.

In other words, at the UV / working-branch level, the 12-mode BCC shell-sum branch more naturally supports stronger longitudinal anisotropy than the one-mediator Class II branch.

\section{1. Explicit formulas}

For the one-mediator Class II branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_g,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_Z,
\qquad
\beta=0,
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa_g=\frac{g_X^2A^2}{M_X^2}\frac{|G_*|^2}{2},
\qquad
\kappa_Z=\frac{4Z}{A}.
}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{II}}
=
\frac{g_X^2A^3|G_*|^2}{8|Z|M_X^2}.
}
\end{equation}

For the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC shell-sum branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\parallel^{(12)}=4\,\frac{gA^2}{q_*^2},
\qquad
W_I^{(12)}=\frac{4Z}{A},
\qquad
W_J^{(12)}=0,
}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{12}
=
\frac{|g|A^3}{|Z|q_*^2}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Direct comparison}

The ratio of the two anisotropies is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_{\mathrm{II}}}{\rho_{12}}
=
\frac{g_X^2|G_*|^2q_*^2}{8|g|M_X^2}.
}
\end{equation}

If one identifies the selected shell scale with \(q_*\sim |G_*|\), then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_{\mathrm{II}}}{\rho_{12}}
\sim
\frac{g_X^2q_*^4}{8|g|M_X^2}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{II}}>\rho_{12}
\iff
g_X^2q_*^4>8|g|M_X^2,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{II}}<\rho_{12}
\iff
g_X^2q_*^4<8|g|M_X^2.
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Natural TECT interpretation}

Because the Class II mediator is introduced as a heavy internal sector, the natural working regime satisfies a large \(M_X\) hierarchy.
Hence \(\rho_{\mathrm{II}}\) is generically suppressed by \(1/M_X^2\), while \(\rho_{12}\) has no such heavy-mass suppression.

Therefore, at the UV / working-branch level, the natural generic ordering is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{12}>\rho_{\mathrm{II}}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. IR qualification}

At the infrared level, quartic cubic anisotropy is already known to be irrelevant in the minimal TECT count \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\), so both branches are expected to flow toward weaker anisotropy.
However, the derivative-anisotropy / velocity-locking flow is not yet fully closed microscopically.

So the conclusion \(\rho_{12}>\rho_{\mathrm{II}}\) should be understood as a natural UV / working-branch statement, not yet a final IR universality theorem.

\section{Current solved Branch-B PDE in the graded \(2+2\) mainline}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}

=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad

=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Source-by-Source Hessian Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O$}{lambda_c,Lambda_E,Lambda_O} in the Graded \(2+2\) Mainline}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

In the graded \(2+2\) bypass route, the only remaining full-PDE gap is the actual extraction of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
\]
from the complete background-dependent Hessian.

In the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch one already has
\[

so the reduced PDE coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad

\qquad

It is the explicit blockwise extraction
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\to
V^\mu(\xi)
\to
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
\to
(s_1,s_2,s_3)

\section{1. Starting background and fluctuation split}

Use the shell-/defect-adapted minimal background
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:G_start_bg}
\end{equation}
or, if the induced gauge connection is retained,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}=(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:G_start_bg_full}
\end{equation}
Expand
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta).
}
\label{eq:G_fluc_split}
\end{equation}
The background-dependent Hessian then has the exact \(3\times3\) block form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:G_block_hessian}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Universal operator split and the actual transport kernel}

The full quadratic operator is organized as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:G_master_split}
\end{equation}

The coefficient point \((\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\) is read only from the odd first-order transport kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
}
\label{eq:G_L1}
\end{equation}

Therefore the first explicit step is:
collect from every Hessian block only those terms carrying exactly one worldvolume derivative \(\partial_{y^\mu}\), move all \(\xi\)-dependent matrices to the left, and sum them into \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

\section{3. Which Hessian sources can actually feed \(V^\mu\)}

At the symmetric point, local quartic potential sectors are generically \(p^2\)-silent and act as mass-type corrections rather than transport generators.
The genuinely viable sources of nontrivial derivative transport are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) field-dependent derivative vertices beyond the minimal bilinear truncation,}
}
\label{eq:G_source_i}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) gauge/constraint-sector contributions in the }A\text{-sector,}
}
\label{eq:G_source_ii}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iii) background-generated effective cubic vertices, giving nonzero }\Gamma^{(3)}\Gamma^{(3)}\text{ contributions.}
}
\label{eq:G_source_iii}
\end{equation}

Thus, in the actual Hessian blocks \(\mathcal H_{IJ}\), the first-order transport candidates are precisely the pieces with one worldvolume derivative generated by these three mechanisms.

\section{4. Tangent-bundle projection and local \(Q_B\)-response}

Project to the tangent bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C Q_B=2,
\]
and choose an adapted orthonormal frame
\[
(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)).
\]
The actual Hermitian \(Q_B\)-response is then written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}(\xi) & r_{12}(\xi)\\
\overline{r_{12}(\xi)} & r_{22}(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:G_Ract}
\end{equation}

Its Pauli decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:G_Ract_pauli}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_0=\frac{r_{11}+r_{22}}{2},
\qquad
s_3=\frac{r_{11}-r_{22}}{2},
\qquad
s_1=\Re r_{12},
\qquad
s_2=-\Im r_{12}.
}
\label{eq:G_s123}
\end{equation}

So the actual transport problem is reduced to identifying the scalar functions
\[
s_1(\xi),\qquad s_2(\xi),\qquad s_3(\xi)
\]
coming from the first-order Hessian blocks.

\section{5. Worldvolume/S2 matching}

The local S2-compatible transport kernel has the invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

=

Hence the channel map is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\longrightarrow

\qquad
s_1\longrightarrow \Lambda_E,
\qquad
s_2\longrightarrow \Lambda_O.

\label{eq:G_channel_map}
\end{equation}

Since the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch satisfies
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
the longitudinal channel is Branch B, so \(s_3\) must be matched to the primitive \(\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3\) structure, i.e. to \(\lambda_c\).

\section{6. Projection to the low modes}

Let the even/odd low modes be
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad

\begin{equation}

Matching \eqref{eq:G_Mmu} to the S2 form gives the final coefficient dictionary

\lambda_\parallel
=

\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:G_coeff_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Inside the exact concrete Class II branch, this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:G_coeff_dictionary_B}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Final executable blockwise protocol}

The actual next calculation is now fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Write the full background-dependent Hessian block-by-block as in \eqref{eq:G_block_hessian}.
\item From each block \(\mathcal H_{IJ}\), isolate only the terms with exactly one \(\partial_{y^\mu}\).
\item Sum those terms into \(V^\mu(\xi)\).
\item Project \(V^\mu(\xi)\) to \(Q_B(\xi)\) and read the matrix entries \(r_{11},r_{22},r_{12}\).
\item Form
\[
s_3=\frac{r_{11}-r_{22}}{2},
\qquad
s_1=\Re r_{12},
\qquad
s_2=-\Im r_{12}.
\]
\item Match \(s_3\) to the Branch-B longitudinal seed \(\lambda_c\), and \(s_1,s_2\) to \(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\).
\item Insert the result into \eqref{eq:G_lambda_final}--\eqref{eq:G_alpha_beta_final}.
\end{enumerate}

No further structural theorem is required.
The remaining frontier is a literal source-by-source Hessian differentiation and projection computation.

\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad

}
\]

More explicitly:

No further structural theorem is needed.
The remaining frontier is a literal source-by-source Hessian differentiation and projection computation.

\section{Final summary}

The correct mainline is the graded \(2+2\) bypass route.

The full remaining coefficient point is
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad
\lambda_c,\qquad
\Lambda_E,\qquad
\Lambda_O.
\]

In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch one already has
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the practical remaining microscopic task is reduced to
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad
\Lambda_E,\qquad
\Lambda_O.
\]

The complete extraction protocol is:

\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\longrightarrow
\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)
\longrightarrow
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0\mathbf 1_2+s_1\sigma_1+s_2\sigma_2+s_3\sigma_3.
\]

At the current solved lowest-order stage:

\[
OO \text{ carries the primitive longitudinal coefficient } \lambda_c,
\]
while
\[
TD+DT \text{ carry the leading transverse coefficients } \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O,
\]
with \(OD,DO,DD\) as candidate corrections beyond the minimal truncation.

Thus the actual remaining microscopic calculation is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to\lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

After inserting the explicit overlaps,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad

\]
the reduced PDE coefficients are

\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,

=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

No further structural theorem is needed.
What remains is a literal source-by-source Hessian differentiation and projection computation.
